Travel Correspondence

From Shanghai to Xi'an (Part 1)

— Geng Ya

"Fly, fly, fly to the east, fly to the west..." As a child seeing off a certain passenger sang this familiar song, the Eurasia Aviation Company's "Junkers" aircraft, truly carrying the reporter and three other passengers, floated into the clouds and soared into the air, flying over the Longhua Pagoda. At that time, the pagoda, temples, houses, bamboo, trees, etc., seen from above, gradually shrank: shrinking into models that could be played with in the palm of your hand. Looking far into the distance, I could see a thousand miles at a glance, reminding me of being on a ship in the ocean. However, the seascape is flat and monotonous, while this [airscape] is ever-changing and peculiar. Below, an endless expanse of newly cultivated wheat fields, crisscrossed by paths, the soil a brownish-yellow, like countless baked pancakes and biscuits, thrown back piece by piece. Interspersed with winding silver streams, clusters of green trees yet to shed their leaves, brilliant red maple leaves, and hills that did not clearly show their height or peaks. The complex scenery and diverse colors came into contact with my eyes, and I could not help but be captivated. After flying for a while, the attendant brought a full cup of coffee and two pieces of pastry on paper plates. The paper plates were placed on my lap, and I ate while holding the cup and spoon, quite composed and at ease—this was of course due to the smooth flight of the aircraft and the perfect internal facilities; let me jot down some notes below.

The aircraft we were on was a three-propeller aircraft (the propellers in the air can turn 1,800 times per minute), with a load capacity of 2,000 kilograms, with eight passenger seats. If crowded, it could be increased to sixteen seats, plus two pilots, a telegraph operator, and a servant, for a total of twenty people. The two pilots sit side by side at the front of the aircraft to steer: the telegraph operator is next to the middle, writing and translating the weather reports sent by radio from the stations ahead, and notifying them at any time. The passenger seats are in the abdomen, just like the seats in a movie theater, with four or five rows (they are movable), each row can seat two people, separated by the window wall, with an aisle in the middle. Above the car window, there is a net pocket for storing light items. A thick silk ribbon runs along the window wall. If the weather changes drastically and the aircraft suddenly encounters a thick air layer and rises one or two feet, or suddenly encounters a thin air layer and falls two or three feet, you can grab the ribbon if you are afraid of dizziness. Moreover, a strong stream of thin air runs through the middle of the ribbon. If you really feel dizzy, you can also release the air ball to blow some fresh air into your face. When the aircraft flies at an altitude, if a passenger suffers from heart disease and feels difficulty breathing, they can notify the attendant to turn on the oxygen cylinder for use. The altitude from Shanghai to Nanjing is mostly between 600 meters and 900 meters. When passing through the mountainous area between Henan and Shaanxi, it only reaches 1,300 meters, which is not very high, but that day a passenger "ugh"ed and vomited out the pastries they had just eaten in the morning, but it did not soil the pure land of heaven, because the seat was already equipped with a vomit bag. There is also an enameled toilet in the tail for occasional urination and defecation.

This type of aircraft was originally a new German military aircraft. The side of the fuselage's chest and abdomen facing the ground (the upper half of the back is for passengers) was originally used to install bombs; converted to a civilian aircraft, it is used to store luggage and mail. But in times of emergency, with the addition of a machine gun to the tail, it can still be converted to a military aircraft.

Just after flying for a short time, the aircraft skimmed over a few small hills and discovered Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum and half of the city circle bathed in the morning mist. Needless to say, we had arrived at the first stop, Nanjing. Looking at my watch, it was 7:16 AM, subtracting the 6:50 AM departure time, the journey lasted only one hour and six minutes. But it is not fast enough. If you take a streamlined propeller aircraft, it only takes fifty minutes. (To be continued)

Tokyo Correspondence

People's Front and Social Mass Party

— Yunnan

Since the outbreak of the Spanish Civil War, the Japanese government has further suppressed the "People's Front Movement." The arrest of many progressive intellectuals, the suspension of many magazines, and the military's ban on employees of government-run military supply factories from joining labor unions are all direct and indirect blows to the People's Front Movement.

According to spokespersons for the government, the People's Front is for defending the motherland, opposing fascist forces, and is advocated primarily by the Communist Party. However, the Japanese government's "rural relief policies," "nationalization of electricity" policies, etc., all have a national socialist character and do not tend toward "fascism." Moreover, Japan itself has not been subjected to foreign invasion, and there is no Communist Party organization in Japan (?). Therefore, there is no need for Japan to form a People's Front. If it were to be forcibly formed, it would only promote division and antagonism among the people of Japan (see Nogi Hokan's "Analysis of the People's Front," *Era*, November issue). But what is the truth? Reality precisely shatters this embellished facade, and the Japanese People's Front Movement is actively unfolding on a realistic foundation.

Although Japan does not have a very powerful fascist party, there are clearly fascist forces within various political parties. Furthermore, the "National Alliance" (one of Japan's political parties) is explicitly aligned with Germany and Italy. The number of fascist groups outside of political parties has already exceeded three hundred. Japan's fascist forces rose to prominence alongside Japan's activities in Manchuria. The main reason for this rise was the intensification of the domestic economic crisis. This is exactly the same as in Italy and Germany. The intensification of the economic crisis often strengthens the opposition and struggle among the ruling classes. Due to this opposition and struggle, fascism arises. At this time, fascism is often seen as a new pillar and a new force for the ruling class.

Since the Meiji Restoration, Japan has failed to solve general social problems. Domestically: the low living standards of workers, farmers wandering on the verge of starvation, the annual expansion of military spending, the sharp increase in the number of unemployed, the excessive issuance of public bonds, and the implementation of mass tax increases are all sufficient to cause the rapid decline of people in the petty bourgeoisie. Externally: relations with the Soviet Union are increasingly tense, with constant disputes over "fishing area issues" and "border issues"; relations with Britain and the United States are also very acute due to the China issue and conflicting interests; and within China, rising anti-Japanese sentiment and the national salvation united movement are all sufficient to make the Japanese people feel the threat of war and feel that they are living on the eve of war.

These domestic and foreign problems greatly help the development of fascist forces. Correspondingly, the government's policies also significantly display fascist tendencies. For example, the "nationalization of electricity bill" and the "administrative reform bill" are all roads leading to fascism. The parliament has completely lost its function, and the representatives are practically non-existent. As for the political parties, their only function is to cooperate in promoting the establishment and implementation of fascist policies. This has become the current reality in Japan, which is a fact that the Japanese ruling class finds difficult to conceal. At the same time, it is also the important reason why the Japanese people must strive to form a People's Front.

In July 1932, Japan's "National Labor-Farmer Masses Party" and "Social Masses Party" merged to form the "Social Mass Party" (hereinafter referred to as the Social Mass Party). This was an expression of responding to the demands of the masses, uniting in a common front, and confronting fascist forces. In addition to the above two parties, the formation of the Social Mass Party was supported by the "Labor Union Council" (among organized workers in Japan, those belonging to the Labor Union Council are said to account for seven-tenths) and the "Japan Farmers' General Alliance" (most of the national farmers' associations joined, making it the mainstream of the Japanese farmers' movement). What is particularly noteworthy is that the "Tenant Farmers' Alliance" (composed of a large number of small and medium-sized merchants and industrialists and general salary earners) also became one of the supporting groups of the Social Mass Party.

What does this phenomenon illustrate? It means that the formation of the Japanese People's Front did not begin today, but only has the name "People's Front" today.

Although the Social Mass Party has received the support of many of the above-mentioned groups, it itself is still unable to develop healthily. On the one hand, this is due to the suppression of fascist forces, but on the other hand, it is also due to the lack of correct understanding on the part of the Social Mass Party's cadres themselves. Some of them even say: "Because the goal of workers and peasants is to overthrow capitalism, we should first unite with the fascists to overthrow capitalism." Such a view has already become a bodyguard for the fascists.

For the sake of the important goals of the Party, the Japanese people have theoretically fully criticized the Social Mass Party, but strategically, they still attempt to expand the united front centered on the Social Mass Party. This can be seen from the unprecedented victory of the proletarian parties in the general election in May of this year. The proletarian parties want to occupy a unified political front to launch a struggle against fascism. After the "February 26th Incident" this year, it seemed on the surface that the fascist camp had already been shaken and split, but in fact, the fascist forces had become even more expanded. After the "February 26th Incident," the oppression suffered by the masses was even greater than before. Therefore, the masses' demand for a unified political front was even more intense than before. The labor unions and "Farmers' Associations" that had previously held a critical attitude towards the Social Mass Party also began to form a unified front centered on the Social Mass Party based on the wishes of the masses.

However, the Social Mass Party itself does not have the determination to unite various forces outside the party to form an anti-fascist People's Front. Even though the "New Labor-Farmer Proletarian Groups Council" has been established, they clearly wrote in their declaration: "...With the goal of forming a People's Front, unite various forces other than the Social Mass Party on the anti-fascist front, and then join the Social Mass Party to form a broad and solid People's Front." But the attitude of the Social Mass Party's cadres has always been extremely exclusive.

There are two main reasons for this:

(1) Some of the party cadres have fascist leanings.

(2) They are afraid that cooperating with the new forces chanting "People's Front" will reduce the prestige of the Social Mass Party's leadership.

This attitude of not recognizing the enemy and treating politics as child's play will naturally cause the disintegration of workers within the Social Mass Party itself, which will undoubtedly occur. Moreover, further, it is feared that it will also cause the masses to despise the party. Because under the heavy pressure of high tides, the People's Front Movement is no longer a matter of ideology but a political movement. Since its strength has already risen among the masses, what power does the Social Mass Party have to stop it?

The reason why the Social Mass Party opposes the People's Front is: "Forming a People's Front will only stimulate the other side, giving the government an excuse to suppress the labor movement." However, this reason has not been adopted by the masses, but has instead aroused the masses' resentment. As a result, a People's Front Movement has formed that will break away from the guidance of the Social Mass Party's leadership and be automatically organized and automatically developed by worker groups, farmer groups, workers and peasants belonging to the Social Mass Party, and some unorganized masses outside of the Social Mass Party.

According to a recent report from the Labor Research Department of the Japan Political and Economic Research Institute, on August 27, with the support of several labor groups, the "United Promotion Committee" passed a resolution stating: "It is necessary to unite all proletarian forces, with the Social Mass Party as the center, in order to realize a unified anti-fascist political front." At the same time, the "Labor-Farmer Council" also issued a statement that if the Social Mass Party accepts the proposals of various groups and opens its doors, the "Labor-Farmer Council" will also join the Social Mass Party unconditionally. The Social Mass Party responded specifically to this request on September 2, proposing three conditions:

(1) Each group must individually declare its support for the Social Mass Party.

(2) Each group must participate in the "Labor Union Council."

(3) Upon joining the party, one must join the branch to which one belongs in an individual capacity.

However, the Social Mass Party cleverly rejected the Labor-Farmer Council. The reason given was that for the sake of the organizational relations of the political party, it must be considered individually. However, on September 4, the "Labor-Farmer Council" again made an unconditional request to join. There has been no concrete result to this day. In short, regardless of the intentions of the Social Mass Party's cadres, the force that erupts from below can always promote the development of the Japanese People's Front.

Current Commentary

On the Aid-Suiyuan Movement

— Yi

In these past few days, our highly respected General Fu Zuoyi, along with his brave and skilled soldiers, is fighting a life-and-death battle against the so-called puppet bandit army commanded by a certain power outside Zhaizhai, amidst the freezing cold, for the sake of the motherland. This kind of heroic and arduous battle is of great significance in the historical destiny of our country. According to information from the front, the puppet bandit army, carrying modern military weapons such as airplanes, tanks, and heavy artillery, has launched fierce attacks on our army's positions in Hongge'ertu many times since the evening of the 14th. Airplanes marked with a certain country's insignia dropped more than a hundred bombs. However, because our army's morale is high, every attack has been repelled. The enemy is now continuing to transfer puppet troops from Duolun and Rehe to reinforce their forces, preparing to continue their fierce attacks. It is said that the enemy's planned strategy is to break through our army's defense line in Xinghe and Taolin, invade Zhuozishan and Pingdiquan, and cut off the Ping-Sui Railway. At the same time, they will send cavalry into the Daqing Mountains, advance along dangerous routes, and raid Wuyuan and Hetao. Judging from this information, it is imaginable that an even more tragic war will soon arrive. We know that the puppet bandit army itself is mostly a hastily assembled rabble, and its combat capability is not strong. However, the international forces behind it have already been clearly demonstrated in the offensive weapons such as airplanes and tanks. Therefore, we must not regard this war as an ordinary bandit suppression war. We firmly believe that this is a war that concerns the life and death of our country, and we need the whole country to respond with all its strength.

This understanding has gradually become widespread among our people. In recent days, people from all walks of life have enthusiastically donated to the Suiyuan army's relief fund. Many scenes are worthy of praise and tears. The suspension of coal use and reduction of food consumption in schools in Ping and Hu demonstrate the rising emotions of young people. Yan Xishan's use of his inheritance to save the country demonstrates the spirit of sacrifice of the propertied class. Moreover, the request from more than thirty groups in Shanghai to establish a Suiyuan Army Support Association is especially sufficient to express the common will of the people. We hope that this kind of movement will develop as much as possible throughout the country, so that everyone will understand that their own fate is closely linked to the soldiers on the front lines, and be willing to cut back on food and clothing to fulfill their own responsibility to the motherland. Because if this bit-by-bit strength is fully gathered together, it will definitely be able to save Suiyuan, and thus save the entire crisis of China.

As for the government, of course, there are already well-established plans for assisting and providing for the Suiyuan soldiers. However, in view of the seriousness of the situation, we cannot help but express some of our hopes to the government. We feel that since the puppet bandit army has a strong backing and can receive unlimited supplies, we must not limit ourselves to local defense in military terms. We must make comprehensive plans in many aspects. Otherwise, "a single spark can start a prairie fire." The rebels in Spain have already attacked the capital of that country because they have an international backing. Is this not a warning for us?

U.S. Asiatic Fleet Visits Singapore Naval Port for the First Time; British and American Ships Exchange Salutes; Dutch East Indies Fleet Also Arrives

The U.S. Asiatic Fleet, led by Admiral Harnell, arrived here today for a goodwill visit. Upon arrival at the port, the U.S. flagship Augusta fired a salute, and the British cruiser Dana also fired a responding salute. In addition to the Augusta, the U.S. fleet also includes the Black Hawk and ten other destroyers. This is the first time the U.S. fleet has visited since the completion of the military port here. At the same time, the Dutch East Indies fleet also arrived at this time. The concentration of many warships in the port of Singapore is truly an unprecedented event. (17th National Telegraph)

Roosevelt Leaves Washington to Attend Pan-American Conference; Issues Statement Before Departure; Attaches Importance to World Peace

(Washington) President Roosevelt indicated today that he does not wish to cancel his trip to the South American Peace Conference to interfere with the domestic maritime workers' strike. According to the President's address to the U.S. Conference of Mayors, the strike may continue for another two weeks. If we compare this labor strike with the impact that my visit to South America can have on world peace, then world peace is naturally more important, he said. (16th National Telegraph)

(Washington) The government officially announced today that President Roosevelt has decided to go to South America to attend the Pan-American Peace Conference. The President will leave Washington tomorrow evening, arrive in Charleston the next morning, and then board the cruiser USS Indianapolis to head south. He is scheduled to arrive in the Brazilian capital on November 27, land there, meet with Brazilian President Vargas for a day, and then go to a certain Argentine port in the evening. He will arrive in the Argentine capital, the venue of the Pan-American Peace Conference, on December 1. The conference was initiated by President Roosevelt. The President will only stay in the Argentine capital for one day, deliver the opening speech to the Pan-American Peace Conference, and then leave for the Uruguayan capital on the 2nd for a few hours. After returning to the country, the President will probably rest in Warm Springs for a few days before returning to Washington to resume his duties. 16th National Telegraph)

(New York) Among U.S. presidents, only Wilson traveled to Paris in 1919 to attend the Peace Conference. Now President Roosevelt is again going to the capital of Argentina to attend an international conference, making him the second president to do so. (16th Havas)

Japan-Russia Negotiations; Border Commission; Issues Still Unresolved

(Tokyo) Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev met with Foreign Minister Arita on October 20 and submitted six questions regarding the establishment of two border committees. Later, he telegraphed his home government for instructions on important matters in the negotiations. Now that the instructions from the Moscow government have arrived, the Russian ambassador visited Foreign Minister Arita at 4:00 p.m. on the 16th. The proposed requirements are as follows:

(1) The Border Dispute Resolution Committee should be established not only on the eastern border but also on borders other than the eastern border.

(2) The issues to be reviewed by the Dispute Resolution Committee include the Jinchan Gou incident that occurred on January 20 of this year and events that occurred since then.

(3) The composition of the Dispute Resolution Committee should be based on Japan and Manchuria as one entity, and the Soviet Union as the other party, with each party selecting the same number of committee members.

Foreign Minister Arita replied to the above items as follows:

(1) Two committees for dispute resolution and border determination should be established in parallel. This is the principle. The urgent task now is to establish these two committees on the eastern border as soon as possible.

(2) If past events are to be the subject of the committee's review, then all past events should be reviewed. However, Japan hopes that the committee will review events that occur after its establishment.

(3) Border incidents occur not only between Japan and Manchuria and the Soviet Union, but also between Japan and Russia. Therefore, the committee should be composed of an equal number of committee members from Japan, Manchuria, and Russia.

The first and second items can be resolved at the next meeting. However, the issue of the composition of the third item committee has not yet been agreed upon by both parties and should be discussed in future meetings. The Russian ambassador left at 7:00 p.m. (17th Allied Telegraph)

Japan's Budget; Army and Navy Expenses; About 600 Million Yuan

(Tokyo) In addition to the budgets of the Army, Navy, and Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Finance has already approved the new budgets of various ministries, totaling 410 million yuan. The new requirements of the Ministry of Finance, the large ones can be approved for 140 million yuan, totaling 550 million yuan. The Budget Bureau of the Ministry of Finance estimates that the total new budgets of various ministries will be 1 billion or 1.1 billion yuan. Therefore, it can be known that the national defense budgets of the Army and Navy are 500 million to 600 million yuan.

The amounts of the new budgets of various ministries determined by the Ministry of Finance are as follows (in units of 1,000 yuan):

Foreign Affairs 17,800

Internal Affairs 288,700

Education 700

Justice 11,000

Agriculture and Forestry 46,000

Commerce and Industry 27,000

Communications 17,000

Colonial Affairs 8,000

(The three ministries of the Army, Navy, and Finance have not yet decided) (17th Allied Telegraph)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Finance has recently decided not to establish a special account for the issue of whether to establish a special account for the study of the other party's financial adjustment payment surplus system to be opened from next year. In the general account, it is included in the transfer payment, and the Ministry of Internal Affairs manages it, with a sum of 223 million yuan. From this, it can be seen that the total budget for next year will exceed 3.5 billion yuan. The Ministry of Finance is scheduled to convene a budget cabinet meeting on the 24th to discuss this huge budget proposal. (17th Allied Telegraph)

(Tokyo) With the approval of the Cabinet meeting on the 17th, it was decided to spend 79,990 yuan from the special account surplus of the Korean Governor-General's Office to supplement the Manchurian Incident expenses. This is the expense required for border security in Korea. (17th Allied Telegraph)

British Speculation; U.S. Will Purchase Silver; Maintain Dollar Exchange Rate

(London) Financial figures indicated today that the United States may make new purchases of silver abroad in an effort to maintain the dollar exchange rate. Under British law, silver is simply a commodity and cannot be used as an equalization fund. It is learned here that the United States does not have this law, so it is believed that the U.S. equalization fund may become an important factor in the London silver market. After the devaluation of the franc, the United States has already withdrawn 21,600,000 pounds from London. (16th National Society)

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that the current world economic situation still requires the United States to use its $10 billion balancing fund, and the president must still have the power to reduce the value of the currency. Therefore, before the opening of the new Congress, the government will decide whether to change its monetary policy to a permanent one. (16th National Telegraph)

(Paris) It is heard that the United States has agreed to lend 20,000,000,000 francs to France. As a result, the prices of various securities on the exchange here have soared greatly. (16th National Telegraph)

(Washington) Treasury officials declared today that they had no knowledge of the U.S. lending to France and did not wish to comment on the news from Paris. (16th National Telegraph)

U.S. Will Open Exhibition in New York; In 1939

(Washington) The United States will hold a world exhibition in New York in 1939 to celebrate the inauguration of the first U.S. President and the 150th anniversary of the construction of the national government in New York City. President Roosevelt has issued a declaration inviting all countries to participate in this event. Roosevelt plans to depart tonight for Charleston, South Carolina, and then board the cruiser USS Indianapolis there for a sea voyage, and plans to sail to the capital of Argentina, and will return to Washington in December. The capital of Brazil, Rio de Janeiro, and other cities have invited President Roosevelt to visit them as well. (17th Reuters)

U.S. Maritime Workers' Strike; Negotiations Begin; Awaiting Presidential; Appointment of Arbitration

(Washington) After consulting with President Roosevelt on the maritime strike situation today, Commerce Secretary Roper declared that a peaceful resolution to the strike seems more hopeful. San Francisco Mayor Rossi also discussed the strike with President Roosevelt today. Then the mayors of strike harbors such as New York, Los Angeles, Philadelphia, Boston, Newark, San Francisco, Portland, and Oakland held a meeting and issued an article calling on all parties to the strike to submit their disputes to arbitration. (16th Reuters)

(San Francisco) Since the start of the seamen's strike, labor and management held their first joint meeting here today with Undersecretary of Labor McGrady, hoping to end the labor unrest. During the week, Congressman Sims stated that there was no need to hold a joint meeting if the opinions of both parties could not be reconciled. Therefore, today's meeting is particularly noteworthy. At present, union leaders still insist on refusing arbitration negotiations. Therefore, the methods proposed by some mayors on the Pacific coast will probably be rejected. As for the content of the method, both parties will listen to President Roosevelt's appointment of an arbitration committee to negotiate. (16th National Telegraph)

U.S. Labor Unions

Tampa - The most important labor conference in U.S. history opened here today. AFL President Green gave the opening speech and did not mention CIO Chairman Lewis, who was newly expelled from the union, nor did the CIO make any special mention of it. However, Roche indirectly criticized Lewis and called on the labor community to vigorously oppose those with personal and political ambitions. As for the dispute between industrial organizations and craft organizations, Green believes that the two organizations can coexist in the AFL. The current point of contention in the AFL is actually the issue of democracy. (16th National Telegraph)

Germany Recovers Inland Waterway Navigation Rights; Britain Considers It a Regrettable Matter; Belgium and Czechoslovakia Promise to Act in Concert with France

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden made a statement in the House of Commons today regarding Germany's abandonment of the Versailles Treaty's clauses on waterways, believing that Germany has once again abandoned the method of negotiation and resorted to unilateral action, which is regrettable. The German government has repeatedly expressed dissatisfaction with the international waterway measures stipulated in the treaty. However, on May 21, 1935, German leader Hitler publicly declared that the German government would hereafter use peaceful means to modify the various clauses of the treaty. Hitler's declaration was notified to the British Ambassador to Berlin on May 3 of the same year. Eden continued, "In order to ensure that the needs of the German side do not conflict with the interests of the countries concerned, negotiations have been carried out over the years, with considerable success." Eden solemnly stated that Germany's unilateral action is sufficient cause for concern and will make the improvement of international relations more difficult. (16th Reuters)

(Paris) According to officials here today, Belgium and Czechoslovakia have both promised to join France in opposing Germany's abolition of the navigation clauses in the Treaty of Versailles, and it is said that Britain and others are also expected to join. (17th Reuters)

(Paris) At the State Council meeting this morning, Foreign Minister Daladier reported on the situation resulting from the declaration of the abolition of the Versailles Treaty's clauses on the free navigation of German waterways and the negotiations currently being conducted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs with the countries concerned. (17th Havas)

German Political Situation: Increase in Political Prisoners, Revival Rumors Again, Active Shipbuilding Program

(Berlin) Recently, political crimes have been increasing daily. The number of those arrested for attempting to undermine national security has also increased compared to before. Authorities believe this situation indicates that the activities of the Communist Party within Germany are showing signs of resurgence, causing considerable anxiety. A special meeting was recently convened, chaired by Justice Minister Gürtner, with the participation of judicial and police authorities from various regions. It was decided that the police and courts would cooperate regularly to crack down on Communist Party activities. The meeting then discussed criminal incidents related to "racial conspiracies," according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

(London) The Manchester Guardian recently reported that there are rumors of a possible restoration in Germany, and Führer Hitler himself is now considering this. "This news comes from reliable sources and should not be taken lightly. It is said that after being advised by close confidants, Führer Hitler believes that the best way to make the Nazi Party's regime last is to hold a restoration. The widow of the deposed Kaiser Wilhelm II recently traveled from Doorn in the Netherlands to Berlin twice. Other members of the Hohenzollern imperial family also frequently visit Germany, all related to this matter. The restoration plan is roughly to have Prince Friedrich Wilhelm (the second son of the deposed Crown Prince) inherit the throne, and the deposed Kaiser himself has already agreed," according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

(Berlin) The German government is actively building new warships in accordance with the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. In addition to the 26,000-ton battleship "Scharnhorst," which has already been completed, a 35,000-ton battleship is under construction. The late Admiral Tirpitz, the former Minister of the Navy, had planned to build a battleship named "Füdenburg," but it was suspended due to the end of the Great War before it could be completed. The battleship being built by the government this time will be comparable to the "Füdenburg." In addition, the government plans to build a 19,000-ton aircraft carrier and many large destroyers, but the tonnage of these destroyers has not been disclosed, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

German and Italian Press Fraternity

(Berlin) The head of the Nazi Party's press group, Dietrich, has accepted the invitation of the Italian government and is scheduled to travel to Rome tonight with fifteen German journalists for several days to connect emotionally with the Italian press, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Spanish Rebels Enter the Western District of the Capital, 100,000 Troops Defend, Fires Rage in Many Parts of the City

(London) The British Embassy in Madrid reported today that the Spanish Nationalist Army has crossed the Manzanares River and entered the Western Garden. At the same time, the government army's counter-offensive plan in the southern suburbs has been completed, and it is planned to thoroughly reorganize the current government, according to a National News Agency dispatch on the 17th.

(London) Although it is undeniable that the Spanish Nationalist Army has crossed the Manzanares River and entered Madrid, according to news received by officials here, the capital's garrison still has 100,000 men and will resist for a long time. It is said that the Spanish government is currently planning a thorough reorganization, planning to abolish the committee and still have officers in control, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

Madrid: It is now confirmed that the enemy army has entered the capital. A Nationalist army unit, mostly Moorish soldiers, penetrated deep into the University City area, but failed to protect its communication lines, leading to a fierce counterattack by the government army. It is reported that they have now been completely surrounded, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

(London) A correspondent for the Spanish Nationalist Army telegraphed that a Nationalist army unit attacking the University City area in the northwest corner of Madrid has advanced, its direction of movement forming an angle with the main force of the Nationalist Army. Its right wing advanced along the outer wall of the former Royal Garden, where fierce battles have occurred several times. Although the government army counterattacked fiercely, the unit was still able to make considerable progress in the Western Garden and other places. Advancing along this route, the Nationalist Army can reach the center of the capital, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

Madrid: Rebel planes attacked the capital three times today, dropping thirty to forty bombs on the city, mostly incendiary bombs. As a result, more than a dozen fires broke out in the city simultaneously. The Jerónimo Church, where the people gathered for refuge, also caught fire. Rebel planes continued to drop bombs everywhere in the evening. The government army's anti-aircraft guns were completely ineffective. Two bombs fell near the Prado Museum, and two prisoners and eight civilians were killed in the Modelo Prison, according to a National News Agency dispatch on the 16th.

Madrid: Last night, the city suffered the most terrible air raid since the outbreak of the civil war. In addition to many deaths and injuries, there was also extensive material damage. Enemy planes dropped highly explosive bombs and incendiary bombs in busy parts of the city, such as the Congress district, causing several stars, including the Provincial Hospital and the San Carlos Hospital, to catch fire simultaneously. The flames soared into the sky, turning the sky red. Residents were terrified by the sound of bomb explosions and anti-aircraft guns. When they began to go out to carry out rescue work, enemy planes launched a second attack, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

Madrid: After the intense bombing by Nationalist army planes yesterday, many houses in several areas of the city were hit and caught fire, burning continuously throughout the night. Almost half of the houses on Vila Alba Street were destroyed. The French Embassy is located on this street, and the roof of the embassy was also blown off. One house next door and one house across the street were completely destroyed. In addition, the Madrid Provincial Hospital and the San Carlos Hospital are still burning. Fortunately, the patients and wounded in the hospitals had been moved to the French University on the recommendation of the French Embassy, avoiding the disaster. By two o'clock this morning, the Hotel Inglés near the hospital had also been affected. Although it is difficult to know the exact number of deaths and injuries so far, it must be very high, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Moroccan Troops Transfer Elite, Artillery Cover Repeated Assaults

Madrid: Our correspondent Chardot reports that the fighting in the "French" Bridge area on the western outskirts of Madrid has been very fierce in the past two days. The Nationalist Army's strategy is to pass through the bridge, detour to the north of Madrid, and attack the city. Therefore, elite troops were drawn from the Moroccan indigenous army, using artillery cover to repeatedly attack the French Bridge. Yesterday afternoon, the Nationalist Army once approached the bridgehead, but was annihilated by the government army's artillery fire. The government army constantly bombed the enemy's positions last night and dismantled the bridge to prevent accidents. Until dawn today, the Nationalist Army attacked again, attempting to repair the bridge. The battle resumed at eight o'clock. The government army's positions were above the Nationalist Army, and they had a high commanding position. For the Nationalist Army, because there was no cover when advancing, the losses suffered were extremely heavy, and they were eventually defeated and retreated to the town of Alavaca near the Casa de Campo Park. As a result of this battle, the area around the French Bridge was greatly devastated, with many military and civilian casualties. The government army has continued to send reinforcements to strengthen the defenses there. Therefore, trucks, tanks, and armored vehicles transporting soldiers and ammunition are constantly on the road. In addition, anti-aircraft guns were set up at various strategic locations to prevent enemy planes from attacking, and many planes were sent to the Nationalist Army's positions to bomb them at ten o'clock this morning. At present, the general feeling is that the Nationalist Army will make a desperate attempt on the north side of Madrid. On the government army's side, discipline has been improved, and morale has been boosted. They have been ordered by their superiors to resolutely resist and not allow the Nationalist Army to occupy an inch of land. As for the town of Carabanchel on the south side of Madrid, the government army has made progress, and its positions have also been strengthened. General Miaja, Chairman of the National Defense Committee, is now stationed in Madrid, but is in constant communication with the commanders on the front line. Day and night, special personnel ride motorcycles back and forth between the front line and the Army Department to act as liaisons. The National Defense Committee has recently decided to hold regular meetings so that it can make decisive decisions when necessary and avoid delaying military opportunities. According to official sources, the National Defense Committee now has various defensive weapons, and the military situation is expected to gradually improve, according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

France Recruits Thousands of Volunteers to Go to Spain to Join the Government Army

Toulouse: Thousands of volunteers recruited from various parts of southern France set out from here today to join the Spanish government army. In order to counter this move, General Franco, commander-in-chief of the Nationalist Army, has sent a Spanish priest to set up a recruiting office here, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

Basque Army Participates in the War, Planes Bomb Rebels

Bayonne: The government army of the Basque Country in northern Spain has been very active recently, as evidenced by the fact that its planes have repeatedly flown to Vitoria and Basauri to bomb railway lines. General Ugo Mendieta of the government army recently flew from Port Passages to the port of Bilbao and immediately took over command of the militias in the provinces along the Bay of Biscay, according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

Spain: Situation of the Court Trial of the Son of the Former Dictator

Alicante, Spain: José Antonio Primo de Rivera, the son of the late dictator General Rivera, who was the leader of the fascist Spanish Falange, was arrested for treason and inciting military rebellion. His brother Miguel and sister-in-law Margarita were also arrested. The People's Front Court here today brought José Antonio and the other two to trial. José Antonio, in his capacity as a lawyer, declared that he would defend himself and also defend his brother and sister-in-law. He admitted without hesitation to founding the Spanish Falange, but said that the association had merged with the youth group of the National Socialist Party, and its purpose was to promote syndicalism without any intention of restoring the monarchy. Although he had traveled to Germany before his arrest and held talks with the country's leader Hitler, it did not involve any political action, nor did he reach any agreement with the country's authorities. Miguel testified that he knew nothing about his brother José Antonio's political activities. After his brother was arrested, his wife had sent two pistols to his brother in prison, but this was not true. His wife, Margarita, also denied it, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

A Glimpse of the Front Line

Western Suburbs of Madrid: Our special correspondent Grant visited the front line on the outskirts of Madrid yesterday afternoon, from the Toledo Bridge in the south to Casa de Campo Park in the west. He personally saw the government army concentrate a large number of soldiers at the end of the Toledo Bridge, five kilometers from the Puerta del Sol in the center of Madrid, preparing to attack the Nationalist Army to the south. However, the Nationalist Army's positions were very solid and difficult to break through. At that time, there were three fires in Madrid. Looking through a telescope, the major streets were deserted, like a dead city. Grant then witnessed five Nationalist Army fighter planes and seven three-engine bombers bombarding the government army's positions in the town of Leganés in the southwest of Madrid. He saw more than a dozen bombs landing and exploding 200 meters from the old Royal Palace south of the University City area. Finally, Grant paid homage to the recent war marks near Casa de Campo Park, where he saw several small pillboxes that had been pierced by artillery fire. The bodies of war horses were scattered everywhere. The traces of tank tracks on the ground were clearly visible. Only a few small trees had not been destroyed by artillery fire and were still swaying in the wind. As for the "Cuatro Caminos" town and its airport on the south side of Madrid, they had been completely destroyed by artillery fire, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

War Reports from Both Sides

Madrid: The National Defense Committee issued a war report at noon today, stating that the Moroccan indigenous army belonging to the rebels once advanced to the Philosophy College in the northwest suburb of the University City yesterday. The government army launched a counterattack on the left and right wings this morning, and the indigenous army units immediately collapsed and retreated to their original base. Another rebel unit had advanced to the Velázquez Institute in the University City area last night, but it had been surrounded by the government army. Until this morning, the government army launched a counterattack on all fronts and made progress. Rebel planes bombed the city yesterday, damaging four hospitals. The San Carlos Hospital had been hit and was burning, but fortunately the patients had been moved out in advance and were not affected. In addition, many houses were burned. Rebel planes also bombed the Unala district in the city twice this morning, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Seville: The Nationalist Army authorities here issued a broadcast message this morning, stating that the government army launched an offensive in the northwest suburb last night but failed. The Nationalist Army immediately repelled them and took advantage of the victory to advance, occupying the Velázquez Institute in the University City area. In total, the government army suffered more than 600 deaths. As for the Nationalist Army, there were many casualties. The government army's artillery and machine gun teams have been moved to the old Royal Palace and the Modelo Prison on the outskirts of the city. The Nationalist Army's artillery bombarded the "Cuatro Caminos" area in the city and the obstacles deployed by the government army, achieving considerable results. The government army is now releasing smoke screens to cover its positions to avoid reconnaissance by Nationalist Army planes. It is also reported that the Nationalist Army on the Siguenza front northeast of Madrid has captured many new positions near Robledo de Chavela. As for the gold stored in the Bank of Spain in Madrid, it has been gradually transported to Valencia. It is rumored that the last batch was escorted by Soviet tanks along the way. This statement has been confirmed, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

German Case of Arrested Overseas Chinese in Russia, Germany Protests for the Second Time, Rejected by Soviet Russia, Berlin Russians Do Not Take Rumors of the Severance of Relations between Germany and Russia Seriously

(Moscow) Because the Soviet Russian authorities arrested a large number of overseas Chinese in Moscow's Leningrad, the German ambassador has lodged a protest with the Soviet Russian government. A total of twenty-two people were mentioned in the protest document. The Soviet Russian authorities have rejected this protest and only admitted to arresting fourteen overseas Chinese, including two women. They were all Russian military spies. German Ambassador Schulenburg is now hurriedly returning to Moscow from the Caucasus. According to the German Embassy in Moscow on November 12, a protest was lodged because it was learned that five overseas Chinese had been arrested. The current protest is the second protest, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 16th.

(Berlin) German-Russian relations are increasingly strained today due to Germany's serious protest against Soviet Russia's arrest of 23 Germans. Rumors are circulating here that Germany is now considering a retaliatory measure, according to a National News Agency dispatch on the 16th.

(Berlin) Regarding the arrest of German nationals in the Soviet Union, a semi-official statement was recently issued, stating that the Soviet authorities informed the German Embassy in Moscow that a total of twenty-three German nationals had been arrested in the Soviet Union for engaging in espionage and terrorist activities and engaging in activities against the "Soviet Union." The charges are serious and German consuls are not allowed to visit them. "The German authorities believe that this accusation is completely unfounded, because the overseas Chinese have been arrested for ten days, and the Soviet authorities have not yet presented the specific facts of the alleged crime. The German government has lodged a protest once and will continue to maintain its protest," etc. At present, rumors are circulating in some quarters that Germany and Russia will sever diplomatic relations, but the Russians here do not attach much importance to such rumors. It is believed that after important German government officials made anti-Russian speeches at the Nuremberg Nazi Party Congress in September, all quarters also reported that German-Russian relations had not changed. Even on the German Army Memorial Day, the Soviet military attaché in Germany was still invited by General von Blomberg, Minister of Defense, to participate in the army parade. It can be seen that external rumors cannot be fully believed. As for the detailed charges against the arrested overseas Chinese, the Soviet authorities are preparing to notify Germany, according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

French Powder Magazine Explosion Tragedy, Hundreds Killed and Injured

Marseille: Two explosions occurred at the Saint-Chamas powder factory here today, killing 40 people and injuring more than 300. More than 100 of them are also unlikely to survive. La Rocque, the director of the factory, also died. The explosion shook the surrounding areas, and telegrams and telephones were also blocked. The first explosion occurred in a talc factory and was caused by a fire. None of the workers in the factory survived. Three minutes later, the second major explosion followed, according to a National News Agency dispatch on the 16th.

Marseille: A large pharmaceutical factory in the town of Saint-Chamay near here accidentally exploded yesterday afternoon, destroying the entire factory. As of now, 52 employees have been killed and more than 200 injured. After hearing the news, Minister of National Defense Daladier flew here from Paris at noon to inspect the situation, plan for the aftermath, and express condolences to the families of the dead and injured employees on behalf of the government, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Moscow: Arson, Heavy Industry Office Building Caught Fire, Several Arrested

(Berlin) The two-story building of the Moscow Heavy Industry Office, which was requisitioned by the Arms Industry Bureau, was destroyed by fire today, and part of another floor was damaged. After the incident, the Soviet Russian secret police arrested several people. Russian political circles here believe that this was arson to destroy evidence of corruption in the Heavy Industry Office, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

Romanian Foreign Minister to Visit Poland, Italian Foreign Minister Leaves Hungary to Return Home

Warsaw: Romanian Foreign Minister Antonescu is scheduled to come here on November 25 for a formal visit. Romanian Chief of Staff General Sassonovich is also planning to visit Poland in December, according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

Hungarian Capital: Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano, who came here from Vienna for a visit a few days ago, has completed his official business and taken a train back to Rome with his wife. Prime Minister Daranyi, a representative of Regent Horthy, and other dignitaries went to the station to see him off. Regent Horthy is now scheduled to visit Italy in the middle of next week, and all the procedures have been planned. As is generally known, the foreign ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary have handled various important issues at the Vienna Conference in recent days. Therefore, the main significance of Ciano's visit this time is only to express the friendly relations between Hungary and Italy, and no agreement has been reached, according to a Havas dispatch on the 16th.

Japanese Police Obstruct the British, British Parliament Discusses

(London) At yesterday's meeting of the House of Commons, Conservative MP Earl Winterton asked Foreign Secretary Eden: "Foreigners, especially British subjects, who go to 'Manchukuo' and other places in Asia controlled by Japanese forces, are often obstructed or even treated indecently by Japanese police and customs authorities. Would it be helpful in practice if the British consuls in those places could warn British travelers in time to pay attention to themselves?" Foreign Secretary Eden replied, "Foreign merchants and travelers to Japan and neighboring areas are often subjected to such treatment, which is sufficient to have a negative impact. The British government has asked the Japanese government to pay attention to this matter. Apart from this, there is nothing I can say to you," according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Avenol Arrives in London

(London) League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol arrived here from Geneva at 9:00 this morning and is scheduled to go to Oxford University on Saturday to receive an honorary doctorate, according to a Havas dispatch on the 17th.

Train Speed Record

(London) The world record for a train traveling 400 miles non-stop was broken today by a train on the London-Scotland-Midland Line. The train traveled from Euston to Glasgow in 5 hours and 32 minutes, a distance of 401.5 miles. Passengers and crew members were very excited throughout the journey. The train reached a speed of more than 90 miles per hour in Tring, West Hertfordshire, and often exceeded 90 miles. The slowest speed was also more than 56 miles per hour, according to a Reuters dispatch on the 17th.

International Business Telegram - Reuters Special Commodity Report, November 17th

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 142 shillings 4 pence, up half a penny.

London Silver Bar: Steady today, spot and futures both up 1.875, to 21 pence 25. India and speculators are buying, sellers are few.

Mount Lyell Silver Bar: Opened strong following London telegraph, December futures rose 35 pounds, to 46.35-47.40.

Exchange Rates

British-American: In the London foreign exchange market this morning, the price of the pound in US dollars seemed slightly looser, while in francs it was still stable. The opening exchange rate between the pound and the dollar was $4.88875, down 0.15625 from yesterday's US-UK closing rate. It continued to fall 0.1875 within the first hour to $4.886875, after which there were no changes.

British-French: The French exchange rate opened up 3 pounds, to 105.15. After one hour, it fell back 2 pounds, to 105.13. No further changes were seen at 1:00 PM.

Securities

New York: In the securities market this morning, there were many purchase orders, so prices all rose. Automobile stocks were the strongest, followed by metals, railroads, and steel. Merchants joining the buying activity and the slightly optimistic situation of the shipping workers' strike were factors promoting the market situation. Later, profit-taking slightly slowed the gains, but the profit-taking before 11:00 AM was quickly absorbed. The New York stock market prices are listed on the left.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: Due to the influence of high Liverpool cotton prices, the March contract opened up 5 points, to 11.79. It then fell slightly due to hedging. At the time of the telegraph, the price of the March contract was 11.73, down another 3 points.

Liverpool Cotton Market: Slightly firm today. At 1:00 PM, the January contract rose 8 points, to 6.59.

Chicago Wheat: Slightly sluggish, lacking interest. Operators feel indifferent to this. Demand from manufacturers is limited, so prices do not change much. The May contract price opened up 1.25 to 115.625, then rose another 1.25 to 115.75. The opening prices for mixed grains were unchanged, then became firm. At 11:00 AM, the May contract was 97.115, up 0.875.

Liverpool Wheat: Opened steady, but fell as a result of no one maintaining it. Trading was very light, with nothing exciting to report. At 1:00 PM, the December contract price fell 0.25, to 7 shillings 11 pence 75.

Situation of the Autumn Exercise of the 29th Army - Nearly 20,000 Officers and Soldiers from the North and South Armies - Song Zheyuan as Chief Supervisor Camping at Gu'an - Military and Political Figures and Students All Went to Observe

Beiping Correspondence: The 29th Army of the Army held its autumn exercise this year, which began on the 11th of this month. During the exercise, there were camping, confrontation, pursuit, and other actions. Song Zheyuan left Peiping on the 13th to personally supervise the exercise site. It lasted four days and ended at about 3:00 PM on the 14th. Japanese military officers stationed in Peiping and Tianjin, important personnel of the Pacification Headquarters, and male and female students from Tsinghua and Yenching Universities all organized groups to go and observe. They returned to Peiping on the evening of the 14th. The details of the process are recorded below.

The deployment of the exercise troops was completed one day before the start. They were divided into two armies, the Blue (i.e., North) and the Red (i.e., South). The 37th Division of Feng Zhi'an's unit stationed in Nanyuan, with three infantry regiments plus a special service regiment (including cavalry, artillery, engineers, and transport), was formed into a mixed brigade, with Brigade Commander He Jili as the mixed brigade commander. Furthermore, the 132nd Division of Zhao Dengyu's unit stationed in Renqiu, with three infantry regiments plus a special service regiment, was organized into a mixed brigade, with Brigade Commander Shi Zhengang as the mixed brigade commander. The two armies had nearly 20,000 officers and soldiers. A general supervision department was also established, with Army Commander Song Zheyuan as the chief supervisor, and Division Commanders Feng Zhi'an and Zhao Dengyu as deputies. Zhang Weifan served as chief of staff and chief judge of the central court. The Northern Army and Southern Army each had a judge. Lin Kaijia, the head of the training regiment, served as the Northern Army judge, and Xu Tingyuan, the head of the education department, served as the Southern Army judge. On the afternoon of the 11th, the Northern and Southern armies mobilized at the same time. The Northern Army departed from Nanyuan and camped at Zhenguo Temple that night. The Southern Army arrived at Gu'an and camped. On the 12th, they advanced simultaneously and confronted each other in Panggezhuang. Chief of Staff Zhang Weifan, Deputy Chief Supervisors Feng Zhi'an and Zhao Dengyu all went from Peiping that morning to preside over the exercise. The two armies were deadlocked during the day, so they fought fiercely all night. The Southern Army was eventually forced too severely and could not withstand it at dawn on the 13th. It ordered a small part to resist, and most of the troops retreated. The Northern Army pursued vigorously and reached the vicinity of the Yongding River in the evening. They assembled in Yudai Town. The soldiers endured hardships and were very spirited. That night, the Northern Army used a small number of troops to feign a crossing at Shilipu as cover, while the majority crossed the Yongding River on a temporary pontoon bridge built by engineers at Xinzhuang. Starting at dawn on the 14th, they launched a general attack on the Southern Army. At this time, the main battle began. The sound of cannons roared, and the infantry also fired constantly with non-lead bullets. Red light illuminated the sky, and smoke filled the air, mixed with the sound of firecrackers. It could be heard for dozens of miles. After an hour, they crossed Gu'an. Chief Supervisor Zhu Zheyuan departed from Peiping on the morning of the 13th. Qin Dechun, Deng Zhexi, Chen Jiyan, Wang Shijiu, Yang Zhaogeng, Guo Zhihan, Men Zhizhong, and Liu Zhizhou followed to observe. They first gathered in Nanyuan. At 12:15, they continued to advance, passing through Huangcun, Panggezhuang, Liangjiawu, Xinzhuang, Shilipu, and other places. They got out of the car along the way to summon representatives of farmers and merchants, inquired about everything, and met with elementary school students. Representatives of merchants and villagers in various villages and towns along the way held small flags to welcome them. Song gave 50 or 100 yuan to the elementary school students depending on the number of students to purchase uniforms. In the afternoon, they arrived on the north bank of the Yongding River. Zhang Weifan, Feng Zhi'an, and Zhao Dengyu came to welcome them and accompanied them to Xinzhuang to visit the pontoon bridge built by the engineers. After half an hour, they continued to advance and camped at Gaozhuangtou, about five miles outside Gu'an City. There were a total of nine tents, set up in the woods of Gaozhuangtou. Before going to bed, the Chief Supervision Department prepared dinner, giving each person a package containing two steamed buns, one cornbread, a piece of pickled vegetables, half a pound of beef, and two eggs. Several buckets of boiling water were brought from Gu'an City for use. After dinner, Song and Liu Zhizhou went to inspect Gu'an City for a week, then returned to the tents. After gathering the personnel of the Chief Supervision Department to speak, they went to bed. Song lived alone in one tent. Zhang Weifan, Feng Zhi'an, Chen Jiyan, Zhang Yueting, and others shared a tent. Guo Zhihan, Zhao Dengyu, Liu Zhizhou, and others shared a tent. Deng Zhexi, Yang Zhaogeng, Wang Shijiu, and others shared a tent. They all slept on straw. Some only carried blankets, while others carried cotton quilts. It was cold at night, and those without quilts borrowed them from those who had them. It was a lot of fun. Although camping in the wild, it felt comfortable. Qin slept in the tent with his head in his hands. Someone said that the mayor was "drilling straw." Qin replied, "This is truly sleeping on firewood and tasting gall." Everyone got up at 6:00 AM on the 14th, dressed, and set off on horseback. At 7:40, they arrived at the position. At that time, the main battle was still continuing. After Song finished reading, he ordered a ceasefire. They turned back to Gaozhuangtou and gathered male and female students from Tsinghua, Yenching, and other schools to speak, saying, "Everyone has come with the army despite the hard work, which shows the spirit of enduring hardship, which I greatly admire. The Chinese nation has a great deal of inertia and is lagging behind in everything. If we can revitalize our spirit and work hard to become stronger, there will definitely be a way. I have no party or faction. I have been in the military since I was 20 years old until now. At first, because I only managed military affairs, I had no opportunity to meet with you. Now that I am also in charge of government affairs, I am also happy to talk with you. I have always advocated that anyone who discusses matters from the perspective of the interests of the country, society, and nation, I am extremely willing to accept humbly. If it is only for personal gain, I will definitely not get close to them. I adhere to this principle and am not afraid of any difficulties and oppression. I hope everyone will exercise your bodies, study hard, and be useful to the country in the future." At 12:10, all the officers and soldiers arrived at the designated location and lined up in a 口 shape. First, Song inspected it for a week. Then, judges Lin Kaijia, Xu Tingyuan, and Zhang Weifan spoke separately. Finally, Song gave a general commentary, which was completed in half an hour. He then gathered the officers and soldiers to speak and decided to have the representatives of the Beiping City Students' National Salvation Association present a large yellow satin flag with the words "Support the 29th Army to Defend North China". Tsinghua students also presented a pointed green flag with the words "National Pillar". After the presentation, the crowd shouted slogans, and the exercise came to an end. The soldiers began to demobilize on the 15th, and some of the observers also returned to the city. Song, Qin Dechun, Men Zhizhong, and others departed from Gu'an at about 3:00 PM on the 14th to inspect the officialdom and people's conditions in Renqiu, Hejian, Daming, and other places in southern Hebei, as well as the Pingda Highway. They will return to Peiping in three to five days. (14th)

Opening of the Qingdao Municipal Agricultural Products Exhibition Hall - Simultaneously Holding an Agricultural Products Exhibition

Qingdao Correspondence: The Qingdao Municipal Government allocated more than 10,000 yuan to improve agriculture and revitalize rural areas, ordering the Agricultural and Forestry Affairs Office to build an agricultural products exhibition hall in the Licun District, the agricultural center, so that farmers can learn from it and make improvements. The hall has been completed, and the opening ceremony was held on the 15th of this month. At the same time, an agricultural products competition was held, with a total of three days of exhibition from the 15th to the 17th. The details of each situation are recorded below.

Grand Opening: The Agricultural Products Exhibition Hall is built in the eastern half of the Licun Agricultural Experiment Field. The shape of the hall is 工-shaped. The venue is in front of the hall, with a platform made of reed mats, hanging with national flags. The four walls are covered with various interesting agricultural products and clear slogans that enlighten the people. Around 9:00 AM on the 15th, people from all walks of life arrived one after another, including Mayor Shen Honglie, Secretary-General Hu Jiafeng, Jiaoji Railway Chairman Ge Guangting, Social Bureau Director Chu Zhen, Education Director Lei Fazhang, Observatory Director Jiang Bingran, Municipal Government Counselor Yang Jinsheng, Naval Office Director Li Yucheng, Municipal Party Headquarters Representative Li Xianliang, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Representatives Yu Weiting and Liu Wenting, Zhanjingtang, Shandong University President Lin Jiqing, as well as students from various schools, representatives from all walks of life, village chiefs, and more than 6,000 people. After the ceremony, the Director of the Agricultural and Forestry Affairs Office, Ge Jingying, reported on the preparations. The Mayor gave a speech, followed by Ge Guangting. The ceremony ended at 12:00, and visitors began to enter for a visit. On that day, more than 10,000 people visited.

Chairman's Report: Briefly stated, "Today is the opening of the Agricultural Products Exhibition, and we are very honored and grateful for everyone's presence. Our motivation for creating the Agricultural Products Exhibition Hall was at the very beginning of the Mayor's promotion of rural construction, which was after the Agricultural Products Exhibition two years ago. Because the improvement of agricultural affairs is really the basic work of rural construction, only with advanced agriculture can we obtain superior production and improve the economic situation of farmers. Naturally, it is easy to use their surplus manpower and financial resources to carry out all other construction undertakings; otherwise, if life is still difficult, the motivation to make progress will inevitably be weak, and nothing will be easy to promote. We have seen that this year's harvests in various places have been abundant, so the farmers' economy can be relatively affluent, and purchasing power can also increase, and the entire social economy is therefore active, especially easy to understand the importance of agricultural issues. Therefore, the greatest purpose of farmers is to increase production, but to increase production, we must apply scientific and technological techniques. Countries with advanced agriculture have various methods for improving agricultural affairs. In order to develop farmers' knowledge and improve agricultural technology, there is often a systematic demonstration, that is, collecting everything related to agriculture, such as tools, machines, etc., in one place, either for display or for competition, so that farmers can learn from each other and know how to imitate, and then agriculture can progress. Chicago in the United States, Brosser in Belgium, and Osaka in Japan all have similar agricultural products exhibition halls, agricultural reference halls, and agricultural products promotion halls. The purpose is roughly the same. In addition, specialized competitions and appraisals, such as fruits, vegetables, flowers, poultry, livestock, etc., are held anytime and anywhere, especially very common. Our office bears all the responsibilities for agriculture in Qingdao City. In order to enhance farmers' technical concepts and enlighten the public's agricultural knowledge, we have also held this small-scale exhibition hall. After a year of preparation, all the building construction, display furniture, and specimens were successively allocated 10,700 yuan by the Municipal Government. At the same time, many items were donated by agricultural institutions in various places and agricultural shops in this city, which added a lot of color to this hall. This is very grateful. However, even such a qualitative exhibition hall is small in scale. Within , it is a period , regarding all displays, planning, collection, arrangement, and these methods, it can be said to be another kind of door knowledge. We are inevitable in , placement, and there are places that do not fit the style, we want everyone to forgive, and , the performance of various systems, is not easy, it is not possible to do perfectly with a small amount of money and a very short time. In the future, we will of course do our best to supplement and improve. I hope that people from all walks of life can give instructions at any time. This time, to commemorate the opening, we will also hold an agricultural products competition. Many farmers from various villages participated, and we can know that the farmers have a considerable understanding of the competition and interest, which makes us very gratified. In the future, we will often do various competitions in different categories, just like modern countries with advanced agriculture. I believe that farmers can get a deeper impression, and can have a good impact on the improvement of agricultural technology and the increase of agricultural production. This will not fail the purpose of promoting rural construction in this city."

All important agricultural and forestry products in this city are displayed with real objects, demonstration models, or adjusted specimens, and drawing graphics to show the overview of agricultural and forestry production in this city. As for the exhibits, they are all excellent, especially the radishes (weighing more than ten catties) and persimmons produced in the Sancang District and Licun District, and the gourds produced in the Fushan Institute District (one circumference thick), and the loofah (six feet long) and cucumbers (three feet long) produced in the Agricultural Experiment Field are rarely seen. (2) Horticulture Department: various fruit pickled specimens, various vegetable pickled specimens, various vegetable seed specimens, various bulb vegetable specimens, various flower seed specimens, fruit tree wood specimens, fruit tree pruning grafting diagrams, horticulture tools, horticulture processed products, comparison of Qingdao's main checks, statistics of fruit production in this city; (3) Animal Husbandry Department: poultry and livestock breed maps, poultry and livestock breed models, comparison of the number of poultry and livestock in various countries, comparison of poultry and livestock productivity, comparison of the number of poultry and livestock and the population in various countries, comparison of the consumption power of poultry and livestock products by the people of various countries, poultry and livestock feed formulation methods, comparison of the import and export of poultry and livestock products in various countries, poultry and livestock feed feeding methods, comparison of the nutritional components of poultry and livestock products, commonly used feed for local farmers, utilization and processed products of poultry and livestock products, poultry and livestock breeding methods, commonly used veterinary drugs, commonly used veterinary instruments, poultry and livestock management tools, poultry and livestock barn models, statistics of animal husbandry in this city; (4) Forestry Department: forest tree seed specimens, wood specimens, specimens of large plants in this city, specimens of forest product manufactures, transportation specimens The main type of wood specimen, specimens of forest products in this city, 1.
