Tragedy of a Fisherman Killed in Nanhui

Fisherman Wang Longkui (27 years old), a fisherman from Binhai Township in the Second District, was netting fish on the beach at the boundary between the Fifth and Sixth Regiments at about 4:00 PM on the 5th of this month. At that time, Han Jingzhou, the deputy captain of the Zhuqiao Merchant Patrol Team, led more than ten salt police officers to patrol the beach. The captain saw that the net had caught nine sea bass (worth three yuan) and took them away for one yuan. Longkui refused, causing a conflict. Then Longkui was dragged away, claiming that he would be sent to the authorities. Xiao Niu and Zhang Alan, who were fishing with him, tried to rescue him, but they were shot and let go to be arrested. After Longkui was arrested, there was no news of him. His wife, Jin, asked someone to visit the team headquarters in Minhang Zhenru and other places, but she did not get the truth. On the afternoon of the 9th, on the beach about a mile north of the incident site, someone found a floating ball cap, containing a piece of white cloth. Jin went to identify it and confirmed that it was her husband's hat. Looking closely, there was a bullet hole through the hat, and she guessed that her husband had been shot. However, she was still skeptical. On the 11th, Longkui's body was scooped up by fisherman Mao Fufu in his net at the north entrance of Panjia Hong in the Fifth Regiment. He reported it to her. When she went to see it, there were inspection marks on his head, and an iron anchor was tied to his back, showing that he was deliberately drowned to destroy the evidence. The incident was reported by him to the Zhuqiao Public Security Fourth Substation, which reported it to the county government for inspection, to arrest the murderer, and to investigate the matter.

Wujiang: Huge Number of Silver Coins Seized at Zhenze Station

Yesterday, the Zhenze Town bus station in this county seized 3,000 yuan in hard currency that Chen Guozhu of the Shanghai Liyuan Money Shop had collected from Yanmu Town in this county, preparing to transport them to Suzhou and then to Shanghai. The police at the station found it during a search and sent it to the branch bureau, which transferred it to the county. The county government has now presented it to the province for instructions so that it can be dealt with.

Suzhou: Comforting the Patriotic Soldiers

The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce, in view of the opening of the war in Suidong and Subei, and the hard work of the soldiers at the front for the country, telegraphed Chuan Zuoyi on the 17th to express condolences and asked the government authorities to provide substantial assistance. The Wuxian Journalists Association also organized donations to comfort the patriotic soldiers on the tenth day, informed all members of the provincial and municipal press circles of the condolences, and prepared to donate money, and then presented it to the party organs and organizations to comfort the patriotic soldiers.

Wuxi: Silk Factory Buys Children to Sacrifice to the Chimney

In Xintangqiao Township near Tingzhen Town in the Second District of the county, silk merchant Bao and others recently raised funds to initiate the construction of a small silk factory, installing 120 silk carriages. All the houses have been completed, but Bao and others are superstitious and must hold a big sacrifice to the chimney after the factory is completed. Before the event, they bought a child from someone surnamed XX, raised him in the factory, and gave him meat every day, preparing him for the sacrifice to the chimney. This cruel and inhumane act is deeply hoped to be stopped by the authorities.

Changzhou: Youth Hits Train and Commits Suicide

Zhang Rongsheng, a shop assistant at Hengyuanxing Leather Shoe Store on Wuyi Avenue, liked women and often frequented brothels. He also had an affair with a female worker from a factory. Because he did not have enough money to spend, he was heavily in debt and sold goods from the store privately, which caused him to be dismissed by the shop owner. Rongsheng was stimulated by this, and the female worker treated him as a stranger. On the evening of the 15th, he sneaked to Zhangjia Village, Mingshan Town, outside Dongdou, and stayed overnight. At about 9:00 PM, when an incoming train arrived, Rongsheng suddenly had a suicidal thought and ran to the railway and hit his head hard against the train. Immediately, blood spurted out and he fell to the ground and died. The scene was extremely tragic. Afterwards, his uncle, Feng Yuan, and the town police reported to the local court on the 16th, requesting an exemption from inspection, which was approved to prepare a coffin for burial.

Changshu: Director Ye Inspects and Returns to the Bureau

Cai Hongxu, director of the Second Shatianyuan Bureau of Jiangsu Province, has been in office for more than two months. In order to understand the various cases and urge the collection of Chengtian compensation, he requested approval from the Finance Department in the middle of last month and took the personnel of the Surveying and Measurement Section to inspect six counties under the direct jurisdiction of the bureau, including Nantong, Rugao, Jiangyin, Jingjiang, Taixing, and Wujin. He returned to the bureau the day before yesterday. He has concrete measures for sorting out the various cases. It is reported that the accumulated Chengtian compensation for river cases in various counties is very large, and there are also many hidden and overflowing fields. The director believes that the arrears and concealment will affect the treasury revenue. For this reason, he has specially appointed Chen Weiqing, Zhu Shaoqing, and Su Ruxiang as resident staff in Jiangyin, Taixing, and Wujin, and ordered Jin Minjun, a member of the General Affairs Section of the Bureau, and the first and second offices to effectively check and squeeze out the overflowing fields, and set a deadline for the collection of Chengtian compensation from each Shatian household. If they fail to pay after the deadline, they will be punished according to regulations.

Nantong: Shuangqiao Crackdown

The bandit atmosphere in the northern rural districts is extremely rampant. After suppression by the security team, a bandit den was cracked down upon in Shuangqiao Town, and bandit Zhu Bailin, as well as female bandits Feng Di's, Liu Wang's, etc., were captured. On the 16th, they were escorted to the Fourth District Security Command for interrogation.

Yangzhou: Head Bridge Fire Burns Nine Homes

At the home of Zhu Hugui, a resident of the 7th Bao, 10th Jia of Zhu Xiaozhuang, Touqiao, 3rd District of Jiangdu, a fire alarm suddenly occurred yesterday (the 15th) around 8 PM. At that time, the wind was fierce and the fire was raging. By the time the water dragons rushed to the scene, the fire had already spread to neighboring houses. Zhu was sick in bed, and there was still a coffin containing the body of Zhu's brother in the house. After rescue by the crowd, Zhu was burned, and the bones in the coffin were also charred. In total, nine homes were burned down, resulting in significant losses.

Jiaxing: Arrest of a Large Number of Bandits

Robberies in the rural areas of Jiaxing are frequently reported. The authorities have ordered investigations to ensure arrests are made. Recently, a member of the investigation team, Ren Chang, learned that the robberies occurring in Yuxian Town, a county under its jurisdiction, were all committed by bandits from the Shui Huo gang. Therefore, the leader of the investigation team, Shen Jianfei, dispatched Detective Li Zhankui, along with detectives Xu Baorong and others, to search near the Three Pagodas outside the West Gate. They seized four Jiangbei boats and arrested ten bandits, including Xue, Chen Xiaodaizi, Yao Xiaojiu Zi, Pan Dezi, Liu Xiao, Xiao Long, Xu Xiaowu Zi, Wang Youcai, Zhang Ada, Sun Lingqi, and Zhou Liu, along with a significant amount of stolen goods such as rice and miscellaneous items. After taking them in for questioning, the bandits confessed that they were all from Jiangbei and admitted to committing robberies in collusion. They also confessed to robbing Ge Jinshan's Pinghu sailing ship at Jishanmen Bridge and committing multiple robberies at the South Gate and other places. The bandits will now be escorted to the district command for further interrogation.

Crackdown on Human Trafficking

According to reports from the Jiaxing investigation agencies, there are more than seventy human trafficking organizations in Jiaxing. However, these individuals are very powerful, making it difficult to crack down on them. Recently, Lao Er, the wife of Xue Pei of Dingjia Bridge North on Beixiatang Street, attempted to deceive and sell Ah Mei, a young maid from the Zhenchang Photo Studio, and Ah Wen, a maid from Feng Changnian's home, to Shanghai. Ah Wen has already been reported missing. After a thorough investigation, it was discovered that Lao Er was the mastermind. Therefore, negotiations were initiated with her while also notifying the investigation team to take immediate action.

This Week —Social Aspects—

— Special Correspondence from Beiping

(I) Disaster Relief Movement

The former capital, Beiping, is located near the northern frontier. Every winter, icy winds blow in from Mongolia, and in an instant, the temperature drops sharply from forty or fifty degrees to below freezing. This sudden change often leaves the poor and thinly clad helpless. After the Beginning of Winter on November 6th this year, cold winds blew continuously from the north for three days and nights, causing the yellow leaves on the branches to fall almost completely, the dust on the ground to be swept away, and the temperature to drop to that of severe winter. Taking only the 6th and 7th as examples, there are verifiable records of up to ten people freezing to death on the streets, including nine men and one woman, with six of them being young adults. On the 10th, another seven cases were discovered, including four young adult men. The severity of the impact of the cold on these poor people is evident. It is feared that there are at least tens of thousands of people struggling with death in the cold throughout the city. This is the cold disaster. What is even more serious, of course, is the famine. In the four suburbs of Beiping, the harvest of crops has been greatly reduced in both spring and autumn this year due to scarce rainfall. Even in normal years of good harvest, these people often face food shortages. In this year of famine, these more than ten thousand farmers have all turned into disaster victims, eating tree leaves and grass roots to survive. In addition, since the large-scale military exercises by the Japanese army since the 26th of last month, in addition to several cases of stray bullets causing instant death, hundreds of families have been displaced and have no homes to return to. Furthermore, the trampling of wheat fields and the ravaging of vegetable gardens are not uncommon. Amidst this widespread famine, more than ten thousand disaster victims are directly affected. In addition, there are also a considerable number of unemployed intellectuals and descendants of the Manchus. According to statistics, there are a shocking number of disaster victims in Beiping, both in the city and in the suburbs, struggling with cold and famine. If relief is not provided soon, it will pose a great threat to social order. Therefore, since this week, the disaster relief movement has been launched with great enthusiasm.

The first to advocate for the disaster relief movement were people in the local media and various charitable organizations, as well as local authorities such as Song Zheyuan, Qin Dechun, and the 29th Army, who also provided strong support. Up to now, in addition to the various newspapers having successively reported on and solicited donations, people in the press have also scheduled two nights of voluntary performances at the Huale Theater on the 15th and 16th, with ticket prices ranging from two yuan to two jiao. All proceeds will be used to donate to disaster victims. In terms of performers, in addition to a few hired famous actors, most of them are reporters, editors, columnists, presidents, managers, and their wives, who personally perform to plead for the disaster victims. It is estimated that several thousand yuan can be raised. Charitable organizations such as the National Relief Commission of the Ministry of Finance, the International Women's Benevolent Association, the Salvation Army, the Red Swastika Society, the Blue Swastika Society, the Poor People's Relief Association, the Buddhist Association, and the Wutai Mountain Puji Buddhist Association have also successively engaged in relief efforts. They have also formed a joint charitable organization to conduct on-site investigations, fundraising, and relief distribution. Mayor Qin Dechun ordered the Finance Bureau on the 10th to allocate 20,000 yuan to the Joint Charity Association for disaster relief purposes. As of now, there are a total of twenty-one porridge kitchens established throughout the city, with more than ten others in preparation, as well as several warm shelters specifically for the homeless. Other efforts, such as distributing rice and clothing, are also being actively carried out.

(II) Anti-Drug Campaign

The deep extent of drug use in Beiping due to its special environment has long been a concern of insightful people. The trend of it deepening day by day this year is undoubtedly obvious. Although severe punishments and even capital punishment are frequently imposed, and there is hardly a day without the shooting of drug offenders, the extent of drug use has not been significantly reduced. Starting from the Double Tenth Festival this year, the authorities launched a large-scale anti-drug campaign, expanding publicity, posting slogans and pictures in the main streets, and distributing leaflets, almost door to door, with earnest advice. At the same time, it was announced that starting from January 1 next year, anyone who smokes, sells, or manufactures highly addictive drugs such as heroin and morphine will be executed upon capture, regardless of whether they are first-time offenders or repeat offenders. It was also announced that there are about 150,000 highly addictive drug offenders in the city. Starting next year, between 3,000 and 9,000 of them will be executed first, and then the effects will be observed. Since October, drug rehabilitation centers have been greatly expanded, and police officers have been dispatched by the Public Security Bureau to arrest drug offenders. According to statistics, more than a thousand people have been rehabilitated. When we walk through the streets, we often see dozens of gaunt men and women tied together in a string by police officers, wearing extremely thin clothes and shivering in the cold wind. These are the highly addictive drug offenders. However, since the anti-drug campaign was launched, more than a month has passed, and there are only forty or fifty days left until January 1 next year. As of now, the implementation of the anti-drug campaign cannot be said to be completely without results. However, the manufacturing and trafficking of highly addictive drugs is under the protection or handling of certain foreigners and Koreans, and local authorities have no way to intervene. Moreover, those who consume highly addictive drugs such as heroin are different from opium, and most of them are very difficult to quit. Drug rehabilitation centers, due to financial constraints, are certainly unable to accommodate this huge number of drug offenders, and even in terms of rehabilitation methods, it is difficult to completely eradicate the addiction. After leaving the center, relapse is inevitable. Given these practical reasons, in order for the anti-drug campaign to be effective, effective remedies must be found for these various reasons. On the 10th of this month, the Beiping Municipal Government held a public burning of highly addictive drugs at the fire station of the Public Security Bureau on Gong'an Street. What was burned were various highly addictive drugs from 684 cases of highly addictive drugs seized from July 23rd to February 25th, weighing a total of 893 taels, 3 qian, and 7 fen (approximately 33.3 kg) of heroin and morphine, including the skin, as well as 2,972 small packets; 453 taels of Jindan, including the skin, as well as two small packets; 1,221 taels, 8 qian, and 9 fen (approximately 45.4 kg) of heroin ingredients and opium dross, as well as 194 small packets; 52 taels of high root; 4 taels and 7 fen and 8 li of Xian Gaona, including the skin; 3,917 taels and 7 li (approximately 146 kg) of anesthetic, including the skin, as well as 60 small packets; 224 taels and 6 fen of lactose, including the skin, as well as two and a half bags and 22 small packets; 72 taels of Quick Zhong Kuai, including the skin; 19 taels and 8 qian of coffee essence, including the skin, as well as 13 boxes and 10 small packets; 40 jin (approximately 20 kg) of similar coffee essence, including the skin; 88 taels of machine-made opium pipes adulterated with highly addictive substances, including the skin; 44 taels of opium essence; 12 taels of red pills, including the skin, as well as 57 pills. The quantity was large and the variety was diverse, which was astounding. When it was burned, the stench permeated everywhere and lingered for a long time.

The authorities have the greatest determination to promote the anti-drug campaign, but according to surveys, most of those who consume highly addictive drugs such as heroin are still hesitant and unwilling to voluntarily enter rehabilitation centers because it is not easy to quit. Even in the face of extreme punishment, most of them are resigned to their fate. Therefore, for the sake of humanitarianism and for the thorough implementation of the national anti-drug policy, the search for effective methods to quit highly addictive drugs is currently the most important task. (November 13)

A Giant of a Tennis Generation: Tilden Boils Wine and Discusses Heroes; Highly Praises Germany's Cramm; Arrived in Hong Kong on the 9th for Performances, Departing for the Philippines on the 10th

Hong Kong Special Dispatch: Tilden, who has devoted his life to tennis, and Vines, who holds the throne of professional tennis, were invited by the Yomiuri Shimbun of Japan to Japan to perform their lifelong skills. Educational News

Kiangsu

Order from the Bureau of Education: Elementary School Teachers Must Not Resign Mid-Term; Unauthorized Departure Will Result in Orders to Return to School

The Kiangsu Provincial Bureau of Education considers elementary school teachers to be direct guides in nurturing children and indirectly responsible for the mission of national revival. Their responsibility is extremely important. All elementary school teachers should fulfill their duties and possess a spirit of sacrifice, seeking the welfare of children and the nation. Recently, many elementary school teachers have been able to settle into their jobs and work diligently, but those who are opportunistic and seek personal gain still inevitably exist. The Bureau has repeatedly received reports from various districts that some elementary school teachers, after being hired, have left their posts mid-term without proper arrangements or replacements, seeking better positions elsewhere. This not only harms their professional responsibility but also greatly affects children's studies, which is very inappropriate. Therefore, the Bureau specifically instructed all counties yesterday to follow Article 70 of the revised Elementary School Regulations: in the future, if elementary school teachers in this province who have accepted a position at a school wish to resign mid-term, they must obtain the principal's consent and ensure that someone is hired to replace them before leaving the school. Resignation is only permitted in cases of severe illness preventing service or significant matters requiring departure. If these regulations are not followed and teachers leave mid-term without regard for their contracts, the original school should notify the new employer to order the teacher to return to school. The new employer, upon confirming that the teacher resigned mid-term, must not readily employ them. If the teacher is employed in another province, the case should be reported to this Bureau, which will forward a letter ordering them to return to their post. This restriction aims to encourage the spirit of service among elementary school teachers, increase elementary school efficiency, and emphasize children's studies. All elementary school teachers should understand this intention and abide by it together, avoiding violations or overstepping boundaries that would bring blame upon themselves.

Measures for Subsidizing Northeastern Youth in Scientific Research

The Northeastern Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education, concerned that Northeastern graduates from specialized schools and above who are engaged in scientific research at universities or research institutions both domestically and abroad often face financial difficulties, which leads to interruptions in their research, has established 20 scientific research subsidies to encourage and assist them. There are three categories: five Category A subsidies, each worth 600 yuan per year; five Category B subsidies, each worth 480 yuan per year; and ten Category C subsidies, each worth 360 yuan per year. Any graduate from a specialized school or above who is registered in the Northeast and is currently engaged in scientific research (limited to natural sciences, applied sciences, and social sciences) at a university or research institution domestically or abroad, has achieved significant results, and does not hold any paid position may apply for a subsidy. (Application forms and regulations have been distributed to various schools and embassies, but the office has printed more copies for request.) Furthermore, as the 23rd year has already begun for several months, the office has presented and received approval to issue half of the annual subsidy to each student for this year. A copy of the office's approved regulations for scientific research subsidies is provided below.

Regulations for Scientific Research Subsidies of the Northeastern Youth Education Relief Office (Article 1) The Northeastern Youth Education Relief Office (hereinafter referred to as "this Office") establishes scientific research subsidies to encourage and assist Northeastern graduates from specialized schools and above who are engaged in scientific research at universities or research institutions both domestically and abroad. (Article 2) The annual scientific research subsidies mentioned in the previous article are provisionally set at 9,000 yuan. The types, number of awards, and amounts are as follows: (Category A) five awards, each worth 600 yuan per year; (Category B) five awards, each worth 480 yuan per year; (Category C) ten awards, each worth 360 yuan per year. The subsidy period is limited to one academic year (from August of each year to July of the following year). Upon expiration, a new application must be submitted following the prescribed procedures. (Article 3) Any graduate from a specialized school or above who is registered in the provinces and cities of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, and Harbin, and is currently engaged in scientific research (natural sciences, applied sciences, and social sciences) at a university or research institution domestically or abroad, has achieved significant results, and does not hold any paid position may, at the beginning of each academic year, fill out an application form (printed by this Office) and submit it along with the original diploma, academic transcripts (students studying abroad may ask their schools to send them directly to this Office), current research or course transcripts, and a recommendation letter from their supervisor or advisor to this Office for review. However, publicly funded students sent abroad by this Office and students currently studying at universities or research institutes domestically who have already been recommended by their schools in accordance with this Office's regulations for subsidizing Northeastern diligent and impoverished students may not apply for a subsidy. (Article 4) After receiving the applications and other documents from the students, this Office will organize a review committee to conduct a thorough review and decide on the granting of subsidies based on their research achievements and economic situation. If the number of qualified applicants exceeds the number of awards stipulated in Article 2, the awards should be distributed to those with the best academic performance and the most dire economic circumstances. The members of the aforementioned review committee are provisionally set at three to seven, appointed by this Office, with the director and deputy director of this Office serving as ex officio members. (Article 5) In order to review the research achievements of each student, this Office may send personnel or entrust related organizations to conduct investigations. (Article 6) Each student who passes the review must submit their application to the Ministry of Education for approval before the subsidy is issued. If the aforementioned qualified students have already received public funding, scholarships, financial aid, or other subsidies, the review committee should appropriately reduce their subsidy amount before issuing it. (Article 7) Each subsidized student shall abide by the regulations of this Office for managing and assisting students, as well as other relevant regulations and orders. If any of the circumstances listed in item 9 of the Provisional Measures for the Relief of Northeastern Diligent and Impoverished Students occur, their subsidized status shall be immediately revoked, and in more serious cases, the subsidies already received shall be recovered. (Article 8) These regulations shall take effect from the date of approval. Matters not covered herein may be amended at any time.

New York Chemistry Professor Ni Speaks on Microchemistry

Ni De'er, a chemistry professor from New York University, lectured at Jiaotong University at 4:00 PM on the 16th of this month. President Li delivered the introductory remarks. Professor Ni's lecture on the application of microchemistry provided a detailed account of its development history and current status. According to him, even materials as small as one or two millimeters, which cannot be tested using ordinary methods, can be accurately tested using microchemical methods.

Shanghai Art Academy Holds Anniversary Commemoration

The Shanghai Art Academy on Caishi Road will celebrate its 25th anniversary on the 23rd of this month and will hold a commemorative celebration. The arrangements are as follows: From the 22nd to the 25th, a commemorative exhibition will be held at the school, featuring (1) Reference works: German prints of masterpieces from the Renaissance to modern periods of various schools; (2) Works by domestic masters: traditional Chinese paintings, calligraphy, oil paintings, sketches; (3) Recent works by teachers: traditional Chinese painting, calligraphy, oil painting, sketching, design; (4) Student works from previous years: traditional Chinese painting, oil painting; (5) Current student works: traditional Chinese painting, oil painting, sculpture, design, crafts, etc. At 10:00 AM on the 23rd, a commemorative ceremony will be held at the school. At 6:00 PM, a dinner party will be held. At 7:05 PM on the 24th, an entertainment program will be held at the Lake Society on Guizhou Road. At 7:30 PM on December 9th, a commemorative concert will be held at the China Arts and Crafts Society.

Local News

American Reporter Arrives in Shanghai from Japan and Discusses Maturation of the Japanese-German Alliance - Japanese Side to Submit for Deliberation by the Privy Council Soon - Hoping for Other Countries to Participate - German Consul-General Still Denies

The long-rumored Japanese-German alliance was denied earlier this month by the German Ambassador to China, Dr. Trautmann, when he passed through Shanghai on his return to his post from vacation in Japan. However, yesterday's English-language Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reported that Mr. Paul Patterson, editor of the Baltimore Sun, arrived in Shanghai by ship from Japan the day before yesterday afternoon and told the press that Japan had reached an agreement with Germany on an alliance two weeks ago. His words were assertive, suggesting that it was indeed the case.

German Consul-General Still Denies - A reporter from the New Sound News Agency specifically visited the German Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Kriebel, last night. Despite the late hour, Mr. Kriebel still received him. Regarding this claim, he still denied it. First, he said, "I cannot say yes or no. I have not received any information about this matter. In other words, if this were the case, I would have received information from my government. Since there is no news at all, I am very doubtful." He then said, "I recall that Japanese newspapers once carried reports of an alliance between China and the Soviet Union, which your government denied. The claim of a German-Japanese alliance is probably the same. Germany has indeed denied it."

Japanese Embassy Personnel Also Dismiss the Claim - The New Sound News Agency reporter then telephoned Mr. Minoru Hachiya, spokesman for the Japanese Embassy's Information Department, who also dismissed the claim, saying, "I have never heard of it. I only learned about it now that you are telling me. I dare say that this claim is absolutely untrue; otherwise, we would not be completely unaware."

Contents of the Alliance Discussed by Mr. Patterson - The Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reported that Mr. Paul Patterson, a reporter for the Baltimore Sun, arrived in Shanghai on Monday (16th) afternoon aboard the SS Conte Rosso. According to reports, Japan and Germany reached an agreement on an alliance two weeks ago. The authorities warned foreigners not to spread this news and prohibited Japanese newspapers in northern Japan from publishing it. The Taitung Daily News (transliteration) was banned from publishing because it followed the speculation of other newspapers and carried news that a certain agreement between Japan, Germany, and Italy to deal with Soviet Russia was about to be finalized and would be submitted to the Privy Council. The Japan Advertiser, an American-run newspaper, was ordered by the Japanese authorities to suspend publication for one day because it reprinted a summary of the news carried by the Taitung Daily News. The correspondents of the New York Times attempted to send out this news, but it was intercepted by censors. The content is currently kept secret, but it is expected that the full text will be accepted by the treaty countries before the convocation of the Diet on December 24th. This alliance is indeed aimed at dealing with Soviet Russia. According to reports, the Japanese authorities issued a brief communiqué last Sunday, stating that there was an extremely important diplomatic event that would be submitted to the Cabinet for discussion in the near future. At the same time, the German Ambassador to Japan, Mr. Dirksen, had just returned to Tokyo from Berlin. After Mr. Dirksen's arrival, the Japanese political scene was unusually active. The Ambassador first met with Prime Minister Hirota on Wednesday afternoon and then held a 40-minute meeting with Foreign Minister Arita at his official residence the next day. He then visited Vice Foreign Minister Horinouchi. As a result, various newspapers began to speculate. The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun stated that if the Ambassador had only returned to his post and made a courtesy visit to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, it would not have been so rushed. There must be other incidents involved. The newspaper also stated that the Ambassador had formally discussed Japanese-German relations with the Japanese Foreign Minister. The Tokyo Hochi Shimbun reported that the German Ambassador's visit to the Foreign Minister was to convey important talks in accordance with new instructions brought by his home government. The Kyoto Shimbun and the Nichi Nichi Shimbun also made similar comments, stating that the Ambassador and Mr. Hirota discussed the matter for about an hour, and that the matter discussed was Germany's policy in Europe and the Far East, both emphasizing that Japan and Germany should stand on a common front to resist Soviet Communism. The authorities initially did not pay attention to this speculation until the Taitung Daily News disclosed the facts, causing the situation to become tense, and then they added restrictions. Although Berlin and Tokyo have both denied it recently, it is no longer a question that Japan and Germany will unite to curb the expansion and spread of Communism. The alliance between the two countries will be submitted to the Privy Council meeting in two or three weeks by Prime Minister Hirota and Foreign Minister Arita. The specific terms and the maturity of the agreement, as well as the parties involved, are not yet clear. However, according to well-informed Japanese sources, the agreement will be "left open" so that other countries will have the opportunity to join. As for which country will join hands with Germany and Japan, it is still not certain. It is generally believed that it must be Italy, as Germany and Italy have recently held talks and there is a strong trend towards organizing a common front to resist Communism. However, the Japanese are very skeptical about Italy's participation. Also, when the Duke's father, Wang Mingnian, went to England to participate in the coronation ceremony of King Edward VIII, he will make a brief stop in Berlin on the way to meet with Hitler to explain the importance of establishing a new relationship between Germany and Japan. This matter has already spread abroad. The Japanese who are not related to the current government are paying great attention to the Japanese-German alliance, wondering what the reactions of countries such as Britain, France, and the United States will be, and what steps China will take thereafter, which they are paying close attention to. According to reports, the German Ambassador to China, Dr. Trautmann, has recently returned to his post from Berlin. Whether Dr. Trautmann's trip is related to the German-Japanese alliance is unknown, but the Soviet Ambassador to China, Mr. Bogomolov, is currently on his way back to Moscow. Both of these events are attracting attention. According to reports, Mr. Patterson is accompanied by his son on this trip from Japan and will take the original ship to Singapore tomorrow morning, and then will go to Europe for a period of time.

Various Groups Decide to Establish the Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Comfort and Relief Association; Immediately Prepare Large Sums of Money to Remit to Suiyuan; Designation of Banks and Money Shops to Collect Donations Questioned

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai and Shanghai Local Association Chairman Du Yuesheng, for the purpose of comforting and rescuing the officers and soldiers in Suiyuan who are suppressing bandits, convened a joint meeting of various groups at 5:00 PM yesterday. Those present included Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Mu Ouchu, Wang Xiaolai, Jiang Wenyu, Du Yuesheng, Huang Renzhi, Pei Yunqing, Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Shao Yanshan, Jin Runxiang, Lin Kanghou, Yan Esheng, Pang Jingzhou, and others. Chairman Wang Xiaolai presided over the meeting. After reporting the main purpose of the meeting, the following resolutions were made: (1) The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Local Association, and the Red Cross Society will jointly form the Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Comfort and Relief Committee; (2) Twenty-five people, including Xu Jili, Liu Hongsheng, Wang Rutang, Yan Fuqing, Li Fuxun, Wu Yunzhai, Yan Esheng, Ke Ganchen, Hu Yunqiu, Gui Yanfang, and others, were nominated as members of the committee; (3) Jin Runxiang was nominated as the Secretary-General of the Committee, and Yang Guanbei as the Deputy Secretary-General; (4) Raise a large sum of money to comfort the soldiers on the front line; (5) Designate China, Communications, Zhejiang Industrial, Zhejiang Real Estate, Continental, Salt, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Zhonghui ten banks, the Four-Bank Savings Societies, as well as Fuyuan, Tongyu, and Tongkang three money shops to collect comfort and relief donations from all walks of life; (6) Nominate Chen Guangfu, Du Yuesheng, Xu Xinzhi, Li Fuxun, Qin Runqing, Shao Yanshan, Pei Yunqing, and others as economic committee members.

One-Yuan Movement: More than ten members of the First Special District Citizens' United Association of this city, including Ge Futian, Liu Zhongying, and Chen Jiufeng, specifically jointly proposed to the association to advocate the "One-Yuan Aid Sui Movement" to encourage the morale of the front-line soldiers and plan for national salvation. The Shanghai Business Joint Association has scheduled its thirteenth executive committee meeting for 3:00 PM today to discuss and implement it. The recommendation of the committee members is recorded as follows: "Regarding the recommendation, the bandit-puppets have invaded the border, and the Sui situation is serious. Fortunately, Chairman Chuan and all officers and soldiers have resisted loyally, but have not yet succeeded. However, the bandit-puppets are moving restlessly, and their background is clear. To kill the enemy and achieve results, it depends on strengthening rear support. Futian and others deeply feel that since September 18th, the territory has been shrinking day by day, and Suiyuan has become the only barrier. In terms of the situation, Sui is actually the throat of the provinces in North China. If there is any negligence, North China will be in danger, and the entire country may be overthrown. Therefore, the invasion of bandit-puppets is by no means a local war, but the continued progress of the policy of destroying China. It is urgent to concentrate the power of the whole country, rise up to rescue, and everyone should recognize that saving Sui is saving the country, and saving the people of Sui is saving oneself. The situation is urgent and cannot be observed any longer. Moreover, when this severe winter is approaching, the soldiers are cold and bitter in the icy and snowy land of the northern border, and urgently need reinforcements. Driven by conscience, Futian and others cannot bear to sit idly by, so they specifically jointly propose to the association to advocate the "One-Yuan Aid Sui Movement," and the funds raised will be used to comfort and support the officers and soldiers on the front line. The purpose and method are briefly described as follows: (1) The "One-Yuan Aid Sui Movement" is easy to carry out universally, and everyone can do their best to serve the country; (2) The one-yuan donation should be collected by local banks and chambers of commerce; (3) The donation receipt must be affixed with the seal of the supervisory authority, and the number must be specified, one yuan per number, to show seriousness; (4) Donors who are scattered numbers can combine several people to collect one yuan for payment; (5) This movement will be implemented from the date of resolution until the end of this year; (6) Please telegraph to all sectors of the country to promote it uniformly; (7) Strictly formulate supervision of donation collection and use methods. The humble opinions must be submitted to the meeting for discussion as soon as possible, and a definite implementation method should be detailed to encourage morale and plan for national salvation, and I can't help but look forward to it."

Song Ziwen Went to Hong Kong Last Night

To Preside Over the Reopening of the Guangdong Bank Headquarters

After the Guangdong Bank officially announced the suspension of business of its headquarters and branches simultaneously on September 4 last year, it has now been successfully planned for reopening with the assistance of Song Ziwen, Chairman of the Bank of China. International Issues Research Association Hosted a Banquet for the French Ambassador Last Night

French Ambassador to China Naziya arrived in Shanghai from Beijing last week, then flew to Beijing on the 14th, stayed in Beijing for three days, and after meeting with Foreign Minister Zhang the day before yesterday, he took the 11:00 pm express train from Beijing to Shanghai the night before yesterday. He arrived at the North Station at around 7:00 am yesterday. The Consul General of the country in China, Boudas, went to meet him. After getting off the train, he went to rest at the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road, and then went to the country's consulate on Gongguan Road on the Bund at around 10:00 am to work. In the afternoon, he went to various schools established by the French Concession Public Works Bureau to inspect. It is reported that the ambassador will stay here for a long time, and will go to Beijing at any time in the future. After spending the New Year in the South, he will return to Beijing.

Welcome Banquet Last Night: The board of directors of the local International Issues Research Association specially hosted a welcome banquet for Naziya at the International Hotel at 8:00 pm last night and invited local Chinese and foreign celebrities to accompany him. Those who attended the banquet included Mayor of this city Wu Tiecheng, French Consul General in Shanghai Boudas, Consul Bulinghua, Manager of Sino-French Industrial and Commercial Bank Barr, Editor-in-Chief of Havas News Agency Tan Shigu, as well as Wang Chonghui, Liu Zhanen, Du Yuesheng, Xu Xinliu, Cao Yunxiang, Dong XianGuang, Li Zhaoshi, He Dekui, Qian Xinzhi, Zou Bingwen, Zhang Jixian, Liu Hongsheng, Zu Jingsheng, and more than twenty other people.

Guo's Speech: After taking their seats, Chairman Guo Bingwen delivered a welcoming speech on behalf of the board of directors, which roughly stated, "Mr. Naziya, the first French Ambassador to China, is a skilled French diplomat who has served as a consul in Shanghai and Kunming, achieving remarkable results and maintaining cordial relations with Chinese people. Now, as an envoy, he has come to the East to revisit old places, renewing old friendships and establishing new ones, which is deeply gratifying. I believe that Ambassador Naziya has a clear understanding of the progress of our country's construction and the completion of unification in recent years. The national characteristics of the Chinese and French people have many similarities. They both love peace, firstly; they both love art, secondly; and they are both rich in republican spirit, thirdly. In terms of economy, the raw materials produced in China are mostly needed by France, and our country is now intent on construction. In terms of technology and economy, France can provide China with much help. Therefore, we firmly believe that China and France should continue their friendly relations and cooperate with each other in order to increase mutual benefits. Now that Mr. Naziya has been honored with a mission to China, he will be able to enhance the political, cultural, and economic relations between the two countries with his economic aspirations and diplomacy between China and France. This is what we sincerely pray for." Ambassador Naziya then delivered a speech to express his thanks and elaborated on Sino-French relations. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves until after 10:00 pm, and then dispersed.

Triumphant Return: Nanyang Inspection Group Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday, Representatives from Various Organizations Extend a Warm Welcome, Sharing Insights and Detailed Accounts

The twelve members of the Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group, organized by the Chinese Industrial Associations Federation, returned to the country yesterday afternoon at 12:30 pm aboard the French postal vessel, General Joffre, after a four-month and one-day journey abroad. Representatives from various organizations in the city went to the port to welcome the group and hear a detailed account of their trip. The details are as follows:

Welcoming Organizations: The General Joffre docked at the China Merchants Wharf. Representatives from various welcoming organizations, holding welcome banners in advance, waited eagerly on the pier. These included Zhang Huikang of the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association, Lin Kanghou and Gu Huai of the National Federation of Commerce, Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Boyuan, and Fang Yexian of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Wang Xingyao of the China National Products Sales Association, Cheng Shouchong of the Machine-Made National Goods Factory Union, Pan Yangyao of the National Products Exposition, Sun Choucheng of the National Goods Factory Federation, Xu Jianruo and Sun Daosheng of the Citizens' National Products Promotion Association, Wang Zhisheng of the Chinese Industrial Associations Federation, Shao Daren of the Zhengyi Society, Cai Shengbai of the Mayer Silk Weaving Factory, Hu Xiyuan of the Arbuthnot Electric Company, representatives from various factories, and over a hundred relatives and friends of the group members.

Disembarkation and Parade: After the group members shook hands and exchanged greetings with the welcoming representatives, they formed a line, sang the association song, and shouted "Long Live the Republic of China! Long Live the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association! Long Live the Nanyang Inspection Group!" Afterwards, they boarded over thirty pre-arranged cars and proceeded along the Bund, into Nanjing Road, via Jing'an Temple Road, turning onto Avenue Foch, to the Great World, turning into the Avenue Edward VII Bund of the French Concession, passing Avenue Edward VII, Yu Qiaqing Road, Hankou Road, and turning into Jiujiang Road, to the Zhengyi Society.

Tea Reception: The China Industrial Foreign Trade Association hosted a tea reception at the Zhengyi Society to welcome all group members and factory representatives. The reception began with a welcoming speech by Zhang Huikang, a director of the association, followed by a response and brief report by the group leader, Gao Shiheng. The meeting then adjourned, and the group members returned to their residences to rest. Given the great interest in this trip from various sectors in the country, they decided to prepare a brief report on the return journey while on the ship and distributed it to the welcoming personnel.

Joint Banquet: This morning, group leader Gao Shiheng will report to the International Trade Bureau and other agencies. This evening at 6 pm, six organizations, including the National Federation of Commerce, the Machine-Made National Goods Factory Union, the Chinese Industrial Associations Federation, and the National Products Movement Federation, will host a banquet for the group at the Bankers' Association. It is reported that other organizations are also planning to hold banquets in the coming days, and the dates are being arranged.

Returning Group Members: The group consisted of fourteen members at the time of departure. Xu Zhaolin returned to China from Manila ahead of schedule, and Lu Qiliang also returned from Singapore in advance. Liao Qiumin and Yang Shikang remained in Singapore. Twelve members remain. Deng Qiyao did not go to Medan, but Yao Ziliang and Li Rensheng of the Zhenhua Paint Company joined, bringing the total to thirteen. With the exception of Yao and Li, who remained in Singapore, the returning members are group leader and deputy group leader Gao Shiheng and Hu Shicheng, secretary Yang Chonggao, and members Wang Gongquan, Zhuang Maoru, Gao Juxin, Li Shenyan, Zhang Zuyin, Xu Xuejie, Jiang Junrui, Deng Qiyao, and Liao Qiumin, totaling twelve people.

Inspection Itinerary: The group provided the following account of their trip: The Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group departed on July 16 of this year and returns today, for a total journey of four months and two days. They visited five territories: the Philippines, the Dutch East Indies, British Malaya, Siam, and French Annam, and twelve major cities: Manila, Surabaya, Bandung, Bogor, Batavia, Singapore, Kuala Lumpur, Ipoh, Penang, Bangkok, Medan, and Saigon. They spent one to three weeks in each city, or one to two days. In addition to their time in each city, they spent thirty-five days traveling by train and ship. The governments of various countries granted exemptions for the inspection group's entry procedures, such as waiving entry fees and exempting baggage checks, to show their hospitality. Various shipping and railway companies offered discounts on fares.

Work Situation: A total of seven national goods exhibitions were held in various locations, each lasting five to seven days. The number of visitors reached over 290,000. The opening ceremony of each exhibition was officiated by prominent figures. In the Philippines, the ceremony was officiated by Mrs. Li Qingquan, and in Siam, by the Siamese Minister of Economic Affairs. In other locations, the wives of consuls officiated. During the exhibition hours, people flocked in like a tide, causing overcrowding. In Siam, twenty Boy Scouts were hired to maintain order at the venue, but it was still difficult to maintain order, as overseas Chinese were eager to see national goods first. Overseas Chinese were eager to learn about the situation in the country. Therefore, the group leader gave over fifty public lectures in various locations, introducing the political, diplomatic, construction, and industrial and commercial situations of the motherland, which aroused considerable attention and patriotic enthusiasm among overseas Chinese, leaving a good impression. In particular, students from schools gathered in the thousands to listen quietly. In addition to serving at the exhibitions, group members were divided into groups by local chambers of commerce and led to conduct on-site investigations. Since the commercial centers of various places were in the hands of overseas Chinese, the investigation work was extremely convenient. Moreover, enthusiastic overseas Chinese merchants provided samples from various countries for reference, providing the group members with valuable information, which was the greatest gain of this trip.

Sales of National Goods: Among the products participating in this exhibition, Huasheng fans were the most prominent, receiving a welcome everywhere and proving to be more than a match for foreign products. Xingye tiles, as an emerging Chinese industry, were sought after by both Chinese and foreign agents. Mayer silks were also popular, but whether their prices could compete remains to be seen. Cosmetics from the China Chemical Industry Company and the Family Industry Company also showed promise, but their packaging should be improved. Seasonings have a large market in Nanyang and sales were quite satisfactory. Knitted goods and towels can be promoted, but market competition is fierce. Grass and rattan products from the forests aroused the interest of Europeans. Paint already has a market in Nanyang, and national products are better than some foreign products, but prices are a problem. Enamelware has a large market, beyond expectations. Kangyuan products attracted attention and show promise. Sheet metal has a large market, but import restrictions are a problem. Fortunately, negotiations have yielded results, and large quantities can be exported. Light bulbs can be promoted, depending on low prices. Felt hats are also selling well, and some people want to buy Huafu display items. New drugs show promise, but advertising is needed. Import taxes on tobacco and alcohol are very high, but overseas Chinese are very willing to use national tobacco and alcohol. Soap, especially scented soap, has the potential for promotion. Glassware was inquired about by many overseas Chinese merchants, but the exhibition did not bring many samples. Yaguang bakelite attracted attention, catering to the consumption of high-end customers. Stationery is in great demand by students. Just taking domestically produced fountain pens as an example, they are rarely seen in Nanyang. Hot water bottles need to be improved in style, because those used domestically are for boiling water, while those used in Nanyang are for cold water. Yixin toothbrushes have won good praise, especially those with celluloid handles. The above is a general overview. In short, Nanyang has never known or seen the emerging industries of national goods. Making great efforts to introduce them, the future is very bright.

Appointing Consultants: In order to establish lasting connections between overseas Chinese and domestic industrial circles, the inspection group, in the name of the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association, appointed leaders of overseas Chinese communities in various places as honorary consultants. These included fifteen people, such as Li Qingquan in Manila, eighteen people, such as Li Shuanghui in Surabaya, twelve people, such as Zhuang Xiyan in Batavia, fifteen people, such as Hu Wenhu in Singapore, one person, Liang Shennan in Ipoh, seventeen people, such as Lin Liandeng in Penang, eleven people, such as Chen Shouming in Siam, and twelve people, such as Qiu Yiheng in Medan, totaling 101 people. Letters of appointment as honorary consultants were sent to all of them, inviting them to take office. All the consultants expressed their willingness to assist in order to promote the development of Nanyang trade.

Opinions of Overseas Chinese: Overseas Chinese have expressed that they are eager to love the country and will not lag behind others. Moreover, Nanyang commerce is in the hands of overseas Chinese merchants. If national goods can compete with international markets in terms of price, then even with a difference of 5% to 10%, overseas Chinese are willing to make efforts to promote sales. The improvement of styles should be studied, because most of the national goods coming to Nanyang are sold to the local population, and should suit their psychology. This is the opinion of the retailers. As for direct consumers, they always want to use national goods but suffer from not being able to buy them. Overseas Chinese merchants also hope that the government can develop banks and shipping lines in Nanyang, because having domestic banks and shipping routes can greatly reduce costs. They hope that domestic industry can have an overall plan in Nanyang, with mutual connections. Overseas Chinese are willing to assist with their greatest efforts. The Nanyang Trade Inspection Group fully accepts the good intentions of overseas Chinese and promises to strongly urge the attention of the government and the public after returning to the country.

Remarks by the Group Leader: Group leader Gao Shiheng issued a written statement saying that the group was encouraged by the Ministry of Industry and the International Trade Bureau, and assisted by Director Zhang of the China Industrial Foreign Trade Association and all the directors. They departed on July 16, bearing a major mission, heading to Nanyang, the lifeline of our country's overseas trade. However, his colleagues were ashamed of their mediocrity and took on heavy responsibilities. Their experience and knowledge were lacking. They firmly believed that international trade must find a way out, and Nanyang is where our country's overseas Chinese gather. Their eagerness for national goods is perhaps even greater than that of the people of the country, so they resolutely set out. During the journey, they received timely guidance from various sectors in the country, and were constantly backed by the country, which was deeply appreciated. On the day of their return, they were welcomed by various organizations and relatives and friends, and were grateful for their warm hospitality. The experiences and feelings are briefly described below:

Enthusiastic Welcome from Overseas Chinese: There are more than six million overseas Chinese in Nanyang, including 1.2 million in British Malaya, 2.5 million in Siam, and over one million in the Dutch East Indies. In all the places the delegation visited, overseas Chinese organizations joined together to welcome the group, as it was the first time that a Chinese commercial organization had come to Nanyang. The activities were grand, and they were eager to see national goods first. Although the group aimed to reduce social events and do more work, banquets were still held every evening. In their words, their patriotic enthusiasm and sincerity were revealed. In every place the group arrived, they merged with the overseas Chinese, and in a short period of time, they helped each other and cooperated, showing the supreme glory of our Chinese nation. This was the most pleasant part of the journey.

Impressions of the National Goods Exhibition: Whenever the group arrived in a place, it held a national goods exhibition. The method was to first send the exhibits to the local chambers of commerce, and then unpack and display them upon the group's arrival. Therefore, this kind of exhibition was actually a cooperation between the group and the local chambers of commerce. After the exhibition was completed, it was unconditionally donated to the local chambers of commerce to organize a permanent exhibition hall. A total of seven exhibitions were held, with about 290,000 visitors. In other words, one out of every twenty-five overseas Chinese visited. Overseas Chinese students had a vague impression of the motherland. At first, they did not know that China also had industry, and some even did not believe that they were products of the motherland. After visiting, they were very satisfied and greatly increased their patriotic sentiments. In some places, the crowding of visitors exceeded expectations, and the order of the venue could hardly be maintained. It can be seen that overseas Chinese are enthusiastic about protecting national goods.

Emphasis from Various Governments: The governments of various countries attached great importance to the group. In addition to providing very favorable treatment for entry procedures and during the period of residence, without any difficulties, the Dutch East Indies and Siam formally received the group in the name of the government. It was regarded as a special honor by overseas Chinese that a Chinese merchant group received such treatment from the local government. The group also enjoyed interacting with them due to the importance of public diplomacy. Various countries expressed their welcome to the group's trip to Nanyang, and conducted informal business discussions to promote the development of international trade. They expressed their satisfaction with our country's new industrial products and hoped that prices could compete in the national goods market. Various countries expressed their willingness to purchase more. The group, being a non-governmental organization, paid great attention to the emotional connection between our overseas Chinese and the local people, in order to enhance the feelings between nationalities. In the Philippines, there is the Sino-Philippine National Association, with the Philippine President and our country's Consul General to the Philippines, Li Qingquan, as honorary presidents, and our overseas Chinese leaders Li Qingquan and Xue Fenshi as the center. In the Dutch East Indies, there is the Sino-Dutch Trade Promotion Committee, with the Dutch East Indies Minister of Economic Affairs and our Consul General to the Dutch East Indies, Song, as the chairpersons. In Siam, there is the Sino-Siamese Association, with the Siamese Minister of Economic Affairs and our Commercial Commissioner to Siam, Chen Shouming, as the chairpersons, with members from well-known figures from China and Siam. The group participated in or hosted or visited each organization to promote the development of public diplomacy.

Nanyang Commerce Is in the Hands of Overseas Chinese: Our overseas Chinese have a long history in Nanyang. No matter where, they have footprints. Based on the hard work of the pioneers, they have created today's situation. Whether it is import, wholesale, or retail, commerce is in the hands of overseas Chinese. However, most of the goods they handle are foreign goods. The mistakes of the past lie in the lack of

Welcome the Nanyang Inspection Group back to the country (photographed by Wang Kai)

Page 11

mutual understanding. If national goods can be priced low, they will definitely be able to compete. Overseas Chinese merchants are willing to change direction and buy national goods. In this exhibition, many emerging industries were eager to become agents, which is a clear sign. Therefore, whether national goods have hope in Nanyang depends on whether domestic industries are determined to join the world's commercial battle.

The Trend of Trade in Various Places in Nanyang: Trade in the Philippines can freely enter and exit, but the tariffs are very heavy. Certain goods almost monopolize the market. Although American goods enjoy tariff exemption preferences, they are still not comparable to the Dutch East Indies. All goods are restricted, and it seems that another direction should be sought for the development of Chinese goods. The conclusion of a commercial treaty is extremely important. In Malaya, except for textiles, which are restricted, and tobacco and alcohol, which are taxed, other goods are tax-free, and the consumption power is large. The market has an upward trend. Siam is an agricultural country with 2.5 million overseas Chinese, and the consumption power is quite large. In Annam, the French government has built high tariff barriers, making it difficult for national goods other than French goods to enter. Therefore, if national goods want to develop in Nanyang, it seems that Singapore should be the main base and slowly develop. In short, the group believes that the Nanyang market is our country's only overseas lifeline, which cannot be abandoned and should not be abandoned. However, the operations of overseas Chinese in the past were individual. In the future, there should be a whole, and whether it is the government or the people, there should be a practical plan and definite steps. All related parties should work together to cope with the extraordinary environment. In addition, there are more than 6 million overseas Chinese in Nanyang who are willing to be salesmen, and success is not difficult, but it depends on how hard the Chinese people work.

Toyota and Other Factories United in Strike Again, Clashes Occurred with Several Injuries on Both Sides, No. 2 and No. 13 Factories of the Nei Wai Cotton Mill Also Went on Strike—Workers of the Jardine Matheson Cotton Mill (British owned) To Petition This Morning—

Special report from this newspaper: The Toyota Old Factory, located between Jessfield Road and Zhongshan Road, with 400 to 500 male day laborers, 140 to 150 male day and night laborers, and about 3,000 female workers in the entire factory, experienced disturbances at 5:30 pm yesterday. The male and female night laborers were just heading to work. Around 6:00 pm, when the day laborers were about to leave work, a disturbance suddenly broke out. The workers shouted slogans in unison. The 40 to 50 Japanese marines stationed in the factory saw that there were too many workers and did not take any action. The timid female workers left the factory first. Then, the workers went across the bridge along Jessfield Road to the Toyota New Factory. At that time, the night laborers of the New Factory had already started work. The factory staff saw a large number of workers coming and knew that something must have happened, so they locked the iron gate. The workers wandered and squeezed outside the gate. After about a quarter of an hour, they finally squeezed open the iron gate and rushed in, shouting slogans. Before long, the lights went out, and the factory was in chaos, unable to work. About 1,000 male and female workers in the New Factory smashed some items in the factory. The factory staff reported to the police station, and the police station immediately sent 50 to 60 reserve team members to suppress the situation, intending to disperse the workers. Therefore, they used batons to block and drive them away. However, due to the large number of people, they could not quell the situation. After about two hours of stalemate, some people were injured in the chaotic crowd. The police feared that the situation would escalate, so they sent about 80 members of the merchants' regiment to the scene. At one point, more than 10 workers were arrested. Seeing this situation, the general workers were very angry and shouted for the release of the detained workers. The Public Security Bureau of the Sixth District of Caojiadu heard the alarm and also sent police to the scene. At the same time, they reported to the Public Security Bureau, which sent 60 to 70 police officers to suppress the situation. In order to dispel misunderstandings and prevent the expansion of the labor unrest, the detained workers were released, and the workers were able to disperse. By this time, it was already 11:30 pm. It is reported that the injured workers include Yuan Jiaquan, a native of Henan, who suffered internal injuries, and Liu Xiaozhong, who suffered a head injury and is currently being treated in the hospital, according to the Dagong She. All day and night shift workers of the Toyota No. 1 and No. 2 factories and the Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 2 and No. 13 factories, owned by Japanese merchants in Shanghai West, went on strike yesterday. The striking workers of the Jardine Matheson Cotton Mill, owned by British merchants, will petition the party and government. The details are as follows:

Labor Unrest at Nei Wai No. 2 and No. 13 Factories

The Japanese-owned Nei Wai Cotton Mill, located at No. 62 Robison Road, consists of four sections: the spinning section of No. 1 Factory, the weaving section, the spinning section of No. 2 Factory, and the weaving section, with a total of over 2,500 male and female workers. At about 6:00 am yesterday, over 260 day-shift workers in the weaving section of No. 2 Factory went on strike to demand higher wages. The 260 night-shift workers also refused to enter the factory. Workers in other sections continued to work as usual. However, according to the striking workers of the factory, if the factory still does not increase wages, they will all join the strike to promote the factory's awareness.

Toyota No. 1 and No. 2 Factories Jointly Strike

Over 5,000 male and female workers in the Toyota Cotton Mill No. 1 and over 3,000 male and female workers in the Toyota Cotton Mill No. 2, located on Zhongshan Road in Caojiadu, jointly went on strike around 5:50 pm yesterday. The reason for the strike was also to demand higher wages, and clashes occurred at one point. A translator named Wang from the No. 1 Factory was beaten by the workers. Several male and female workers were injured and arrested. After the Caojiadu Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau made great efforts to suppress the situation, it was pacified. All workers have now left the factory. Also, all workers of the Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 13, located on Robison Road, did not enter the factory after the day shift workers left work at 5:30 pm yesterday and have gone on strike.

Disputes Brewing in Other Factories

There are many Japanese-owned cotton mills in Shanghai West, including the Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 1 and No. 2 at No. 62 Robison Road, the No. 3 and No. 4 at No. 19 West Suzhou Road, the No. 5, No. 6, and No. 7 at No. 14 West Suzhou Road, the No. 8 at No. 1286 Gordon Road, the No. 9 at No. 640 Mohawk Road, the Gongda No. 3 at No. 38 Jessfield Road, the Gongda No. 2 at No. 60 Singapore Road, the Jardine Matheson Cotton Mill No. 1, No. 2, and No. 3 on Weihai Road, the Tongyu No. 1 on Gordon Road, and the Rihua Factory at No. 98 Robison Road. Workers of Japanese-owned cotton mills have put forward demands, such as universal wage increases. The factory is trying to eliminate the potential unrest.

Hua Concession Authorities Closely Guarding

Since the labor unrest occurred at the Nei Wai Cotton Mill No. 2 and the Toyota Cotton Mill No. 1, Tan Baoshou, the head of the Caojiadu Public Security Branch, has often led more than 40 armed policemen to be stationed inside and outside the factory for strict protection, and sent more than 10 policemen to protect the Japanese cotton mills in the vicinity. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau sent more than 60 policemen, riding in two trucks, to set up posts at the entrance of the factory. The Gordon Road patrol room of the Concession also sent dozens of Chinese and Western detectives and two red police cars, parked at the factory gate, to strictly guard for protection.

Jardine Matheson Workers Petition the Party and Government

Over 300 workers of the New Jardine Matheson Cotton Mill on Weihai Road in Yangshupu went on a general strike after opposing the foreman's exploitation of wages. They put forward seven demands, but the factory has not yet responded, so the workers continued to strike. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 pm, more than 100 male and female workers went to the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions to petition for relief. The director, Wan Banghe, received them and promised to investigate the truth and then mediate. The workers of the factory will go to the party and government agencies separately at 10:00 am this morning to petition for assistance.

Two Notices Issued by the Bankers' Association

Income Tax Subcommittee Members　　One-Day Campaign for All Banks

After the Shanghai Bankers' Association's 15th Executive Committee meeting on the 13th of this month resolved to organize an Income Tax Subcommittee, it has sent letters to various banks to recommend representatives. Once the representatives are recommended, Pan Jiufen of the Bank of China will convene the first committee meeting to study the issue. As for the one-day campaign, it has also been sent to various banks for compliance after it was approved. The two notices are recorded below: (1) To the respected, Since the promulgation of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations, the association has submitted to the Bank Association to organize a special committee to discuss and study the matter, and has solicited opinions from the various banks and local associations. As of now, the Bank Association has drafted an entire opinion, and many local associations have also replied. As the tax collection is imminent, it was submitted to the Executive Committee meeting for discussion today (13th). It was resolved that a subcommittee should be organized to carefully review and revise the opinions in order to form a perfect opinion for the Ministry of Finance to adopt. It is now estimated that the China, Communications, Zhejiang Industrial, Shanghai, Mainland, Central South, Jin Cheng, Si Ming, National Goods, National China, Central Exchange, Reclamation, China Agricultural and Industrial, and Salt industries, a total of fifteen banks, will each recommend one representative to jointly organize the committee, and the Bank of China will be the convener. For this reason, the case records have been sent to various banks. It is hoped that the names of the representatives will be determined quickly and returned for convening a meeting. (2) To the respected, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc., initiated the movement to contribute one day to the country and sent letters to the various trade associations to actively promote it. The method is that the stores will appropriately contribute a portion of their one-day business income, and the store employees and association staff will contribute all of their one-day salary income to the government for purchasing aircraft for birthday celebrations. Most trade associations have responded and followed. The association submitted it to the Executive Committee meeting for discussion and resolution on the 13th of this month. Since it is a matter of enriching the national defense movement, it should be imitated. However, it is difficult to calculate the bank's monthly business income. It is now decided to only contribute one day's salary of the staff to the government. For this reason, the notices have been sent to various banks for compliance. Please transfer the payments to the association for remittance to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Xiong Xiling Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

To Pay Condolences for Duan Qirui's Funeral

Mr. Xiong Xiling, a member of the National Government Disaster Relief Committee, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:40 am on the Shanghai-Ping train. In the afternoon, at about 3:00 pm, he went to Avenue Joffre to pay condolences for Duan Qirui. Mr. Xiong plans to stay in Shanghai for two or three weeks and will return to Ping after Duan's memorial service.

Women's Circles in This City Initiate Assistance to Spanish Women and Children

The Spanish Civil War has been going on for a long time, and the suffering of women and children is rare in history. The current siege of Madrid by the rebel army is particularly cruel. Based on the principles of international justice and humanitarian sympathy, the women's circles in this city have contacted many people to launch a movement to aid Spanish women and children. In the past few days, the signatories have included Soong Ching-ling, Shi Liang, Xu Guangping, Bai Wei, Shen Zijiu, Hu Ziying, Li Lan, Ou Cha, Shi Yifan, Du Junhui, Chen Boer, Dong Zhujun, and Luo Shuzhang, totaling over 30 people. It is reported that they will send representatives to visit the Spanish Chargé d'Affaires in Shanghai in the next few days, requesting that a message of condolence be forwarded back to their country. At the same time, they will engage in fundraising for practical assistance. A declaration has been drafted, calling on women and compatriots across the country to unite in assisting the Spanish government and people. Chinese women should especially learn from the spirit of Western women who sacrifice for their country.

Gu Zhuxuan, formerly the head of the Tianchan Stage from Yancheng, president of the Jianghuai Association of Shanghai Fellow Provincials, was accused by Zhao Guangfu, a convict sentenced to life imprisonment for the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, the former manager of the Great World Amusement Park, of instigating the assassination. At Guangci Hospital

Filed Indictment for Instruction of Perjury

Against the Gu Zhuxuan and Gu Songmao brothers in the same court's criminal division. Judge Li Changnian opened several court sessions but could not conclude the case. Thorough Investigation

Rejected the Ruling

Assassination of Shao Wenbin - Criminals Sentenced

Qian Er committed - Another Case - Transferred to the Public Concession

Shao Wenbin from Pudong, also known as Ma Fu A'liu, was originally a groom who later switched to singing Tan Huang opera and then to operating an open flower lottery. Due to competition for profits in the lottery business, at 8:00 PM on July 28th of the 12th year of the Republic of China, he was assassinated in front of 21 Huageguo Road in the French Concession. At the time, detectives chased the assassins and killed one on the spot. The rest escaped. Later, the French police arrested Zhang Narong, an accomplice, and sent him to the Second Special Court. After the first instance, Zhang was sentenced to life imprisonment. Zhang confessed during the original trial that the assassination was planned by Cao A'wu, Shi Laohu, Lu Laoqi, and Zhao Liansheng, and carried out by Wang Shilong, who was at large. The French police then ordered their arrest. It was not until September 2nd of this year that Wang Shilong (41 years old, from Danyang, resident of 58 Fuxing Lane, 920 Xinzha Road) was arrested. Wang then confessed that his accomplice was Qian A'jin, also known as Ma Pi A'jin (50 years old, local resident, resident of 70 Yongping Lane, Megan Road). The detectives then arrested Qian. After the investigation, the prosecutors filed a joint indictment with the Second Special Court for murder and running a gambling flower lottery. Court President Wang Gangxu opened several court sessions to examine the evidence, question the witnesses, and hold debate before scheduling the sentencing. All of this was reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, President Wang presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Wang Shilong as a repeat offender for joint murder to fourteen years of imprisonment and deprivation of civil rights for ten years. Wang was sentenced as a repeat offender for jointly intending to profit from running a gambling den to two years of imprisonment. The sentences will be served for fifteen years with a ten-year deprivation of civil rights. Qian A'jin was sentenced as a repeat offender for jointly intending to profit from running a gambling den to two years of imprisonment and fined 500 yuan. The fine can be converted to labor at a rate of three yuan per day. The murder charges were acquitted. However, since Wang and Qian had committed crimes in the Public Concession, the Public Police Station had previously petitioned the Special Court to prepare a document to the Second Special Court requesting transfer of the two individuals to the Public Concession for sentencing. After the judgment was handed down, the Public Police Station did not send anyone to take custody of the defendants. The judge ordered the defendants to be held pending verification.
